# Skill Execution Specification

---
skill_id: proposal-section-traceability-check
purpose_summary: >
  Verify that every material claim in a proposal section is traceable to a named
  Tier 1–4 source, flagging unattributed assertions and applying
  Confirmed/Inferred/Assumed/Unresolved status to each claim.
used_by_agents:
  - excellence_writer
  - impact_writer
  - implementation_writer
  - proposal_integrator
  - evaluator_reviewer
  - revision_integrator
  - traceability_auditor
reads_from:
  - docs/tier5_deliverables/proposal_sections/
  - docs/tier1_normative_framework/extracted/
  - docs/tier2a_instrument_schemas/extracted/
  - docs/tier2b_topic_and_call_sources/extracted/
  - docs/tier3_project_instantiation/
writes_to:
  - docs/tier4_orchestration_state/validation_reports/
constitutional_constraints:
  - "Unattributed claims must be flagged, not silently accepted as Confirmed"
  - "Confirmed status requires naming the specific source artifact"
---

## Input Access (TAPM Mode)

This skill executes in Tool-Augmented Prompt Mode (TAPM). Read the files listed
below from disk using the Read tool. The primary audit target is supplied via
`caller_context["artifact_path"]` by the agent runtime.

**Declared input files to read (in order):**
1. The artifact at `artifact_path` (from caller_context) -- the section or assembled draft to audit
2. Tier 1-4 reference files -- read on demand to verify traceability of material claims:
   - `docs/tier1_normative_framework/extracted/` (use Glob to discover, then Read)
   - `docs/tier2a_instrument_schemas/extracted/` (use Glob to discover, then Read)
   - `docs/tier2b_topic_and_call_sources/extracted/` (use Glob to discover, then Read)
   - `docs/tier3_project_instantiation/` (use Glob to discover, then Read relevant files)

**Boundary constraints:**
- Do not read files outside the declared input set.
- Do not assume implicit context or reconstruct inputs from memory.
- Read the artifact_path file first, then read reference files as needed to verify claims.
- Base all traceability judgments ONLY on retrieved file content.

Return a SINGLE valid JSON object matching the output schema below.
Do not include explanations outside the JSON.

## Canonical Inputs and Outputs

### Inputs

| Path | Artifact / Content | Fields Extracted | Schema ID | Purpose |
|------|--------------------|-----------------|-----------|---------|
| `caller_context["artifact_path"]` (section mode) | Individual proposal section JSON file (excellence_section.json, impact_section.json, or implementation_section.json) resolved by agent_runtime from `_NODE_PRIMARY_AUDITABLE_ARTIFACT` | content or sub_sections[].content (full section text); validation_status.claim_statuses[]; traceability_footer.primary_sources[] | `orch.tier5.excellence_section.v1`, `orch.tier5.impact_section.v1`, `orch.tier5.implementation_section.v1`, or `orch.tier5.proposal_section.v1` | The single proposal section under audit; material claims are extracted from content and their stated source references in traceability_footer are verified against Tier 1-4 artifacts |
| `caller_context["artifact_path"]` (assembled mode) | part_b_assembled_draft.json — canonical Tier 5 artifact | sections[].section_id, artifact_path; consistency_log[] | `orch.tier5.part_b_assembled_draft.v1` | Provides the assembly index and consistency log; used when performing cross-section traceability audit on the assembled draft |
| `docs/tier1_normative_framework/extracted/` | Tier 1 extracted rule and compliance files | Rule entries with source references; compliance requirements; legal constraints | N/A — Tier 1 extracted directory | Reference set for verifying claims attributed to Tier 1 (legislation, programme guidance, grant architecture); Confirmed status requires naming a specific file from this directory |
| `docs/tier2a_instrument_schemas/extracted/` | Tier 2A extracted files (section_schema_registry.json, evaluator_expectation_registry.json) | Section schema entries; evaluation criteria entries | N/A — Tier 2A extracted directory | Reference set for claims attributed to instrument schema or evaluation criteria; Confirmed status requires naming a specific Tier 2A extracted file |
| `docs/tier2b_topic_and_call_sources/extracted/` | Tier 2B extracted files (call_constraints, expected_outcomes, expected_impacts, scope_requirements, eligibility_conditions, evaluation_priority_weights) | All extracted call requirement entries | N/A — Tier 2B extracted directory | Reference set for claims attributed to call or topic requirements; Confirmed status requires naming a specific Tier 2B extracted file and entry |
| `docs/tier3_project_instantiation/` | Tier 3 project data (all subdirectories: project_brief/, consortium/, call_binding/, architecture_inputs/) | Project facts: partner names, capabilities, objectives, outcomes, impacts, WP seeds, risks | N/A — Tier 3 root directory (semantic scope root) | Reference set for project-specific claims; every partner name, capability, objective, or project fact in the proposal must be traceable to a specific Tier 3 file |

| Path | Artifact | Schema ID | Required Fields (from artifact_schema_specification.yaml) | run_id Required | Derivation Source |
|------|----------|-----------|----------------------------------------------------------|-----------------|-------------------|
| `docs/tier4_orchestration_state/validation_reports/` | Per-invocation traceability report file (e.g., `traceability_<section_id>_<timestamp>.json`) | N/A — validation report | report_id; skill_id: "proposal-section-traceability-check"; invoking_agent; run_id_reference; section_id_audited; claim_audit_results (array: claim_id, claim_summary, status[confirmed/inferred/assumed/unresolved], source_ref, flag_reason); summary (total_claims, confirmed, inferred, assumed, unresolved); no_unsupported_claims_declaration boolean; timestamp | No — validation reports are not phase output canonical artifacts | claim_audit_results: each claim extracted from section content; status assigned based on whether source_ref in traceability_footer points to an actual entry in Tier 1–4 artifacts; unattributed claims receive status: unresolved and flag_reason: "no source reference provided" |

## Execution Specification

### 1. Input Validation Sequence

- Step 1.1: **Determine audit mode.** The invoking agent supplies `caller_context["artifact_path"]` — the repo-relative path to the primary artifact to audit. This is the authoritative audit target. Determine the mode from the path:
  - If `artifact_path` ends with `excellence_section.json`, `impact_section.json`, or `implementation_section.json`: **section mode**. The skill audits only that single section file.
  - If `artifact_path` ends with `part_b_assembled_draft.json`: **assembled mode**. The skill audits the assembled draft and all sections it references.
  - If `artifact_path` is absent or empty: return SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="MISSING_INPUT", failure_reason="artifact_path required in caller_context — the agent runtime must inject it") and halt.
- Step 1.2 (section mode): Confirm the section file exists at the `artifact_path`. If absent: return SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="MISSING_INPUT", failure_reason="Proposal section file <artifact_path> not found") and halt.
- Step 1.3 (assembled mode): Confirm `artifact_path` exists with `schema_id` = "orch.tier5.part_b_assembled_draft.v1". If absent or schema mismatch: return SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="MISSING_INPUT", failure_reason="part_b_assembled_draft.json not found or schema mismatch") and halt. Extract `sections[].artifact_path` list; confirm each path exists.
- Step 1.4: Schema conformance check for each section file to be audited — confirm `schema_id` is one of the accepted section schemas: "orch.tier5.proposal_section.v1", "orch.tier5.excellence_section.v1", "orch.tier5.impact_section.v1", or "orch.tier5.implementation_section.v1". If mismatch: record as a traceability failure for that section and continue.
- Step 1.5: Confirm at least one Tier 1–4 reference directory is accessible: `docs/tier1_normative_framework/extracted/`, `docs/tier2a_instrument_schemas/extracted/`, `docs/tier2b_topic_and_call_sources/extracted/`, `docs/tier3_project_instantiation/`. If none are accessible: return SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="MISSING_INPUT", failure_reason="No Tier 1–4 reference artifacts accessible for traceability verification") and halt.

### 2. Core Processing Logic

- Step 2.1: For each section file to be audited, extract:
  - `content`: the full section text.
  - `validation_status.claim_statuses[]`: the pre-existing claim status array (if present).
  - `traceability_footer.primary_sources[]`: the declared source references.
- Step 2.2: **Material claim extraction** — from the `content` field, identify all material claims. A material claim is any of the following:
  - An assertion about a project fact: partner name, partner capability, consortium composition, project objective, approach, methodology, work package, deliverable, or timeline.
  - An assertion about call requirements: expected outcome, expected impact, scope requirement, eligibility condition.
  - An assertion about instrument requirements: section structure, page limit, evaluation criterion.
  - A quantitative or descriptive claim about project results, impacts, or KPIs.
  - Exclude: headings, cross-references (e.g., "as described in Section 2"), acknowledgement boilerplate.
  - Assign each material claim a `claim_id` (unique per section, e.g., "C1", "C2", ...) and a `claim_summary` (short descriptive string of what is being claimed).
- Step 2.3: For each material claim, evaluate traceability:
  - Step 2.3.1: Check whether `traceability_footer.primary_sources[]` contains a source reference that could reasonably be attributed to this claim. A source reference matches if: the `source_path` references a Tier 1–4 artifact and the `relevant_fields` (if present) or the source artifact's content domain is consistent with the claim subject matter.
  - Step 2.3.2: If a source reference is found, attempt to verify it: check whether the referenced path exists in the repository and whether the content of that file contains information consistent with the claim. This is a logical consistency check — does the named source plausibly support this claim?
  - Step 2.3.3: Assign status using the following criteria exactly:
    - **Confirmed**: A `primary_sources[]` entry references a specific Tier 1–4 artifact path that exists, AND the content of that artifact is directly consistent with the claim (the claim accurately represents what the source says). Both conditions required.
    - **Inferred**: A `primary_sources[]` entry references a Tier 1–4 artifact, AND the claim is a logical derivation from that source (not a direct statement). The derivation chain must be stateable: "Source [X] states [Y]; the claim derives [Z] from [Y] by [reasoning]". The derivation chain must be recorded in `source_ref`.
    - **Assumed**: No source reference is provided in `primary_sources[]`, but the claim is structurally expected (e.g., a generic statement about EU project management that no Tier 1–4 source needs to validate). The assumption must be explicitly declared — it is not silently treated as Confirmed. The `assumption_declared` flag must be set to true in `validation_status.claim_statuses[]` if present.
    - **Unresolved**: No source reference is provided AND the claim is about a project fact (partner capability, specific objective, specific outcome, or specific metric) — these cannot be Assumed and must have a Tier 3 source. OR: a source reference is provided but the referenced file does not exist or the content of the referenced file contradicts the claim. Flag reason must explain which condition applies.
- Step 2.4: Determine `no_unsupported_claims_declaration`: set to true only if ALL material claims have status Confirmed or Inferred (no Assumed or Unresolved claims remain). Set to false if any Assumed or Unresolved claims exist.
- Step 2.5: Build `claim_audit_results` array: one entry per material claim from Step 2.2.
- Step 2.6: Compute summary: `total_claims`, `confirmed` count, `inferred` count, `assumed` count, `unresolved` count.

### 3. Output Construction

**Traceability report file (e.g., `traceability_<section_id>_<agent_id>_<timestamp>.json`):**
- `report_id`: `"traceability_<section_id>_<agent_id>_<ISO8601_timestamp>"`
- `skill_id`: `"proposal-section-traceability-check"`
- `invoking_agent`: from agent context
- `run_id_reference`: from agent context
- `section_id_audited`: the section_id being audited (or "all_sections" for assembled draft mode)
- `claim_audit_results`: derived from Step 2.5 — array of `{claim_id, claim_summary, status (confirmed/inferred/assumed/unresolved), source_ref, flag_reason}`
- `summary`: derived from Step 2.6 — `{total_claims, confirmed, inferred, assumed, unresolved}`
- `no_unsupported_claims_declaration`: derived from Step 2.4 — boolean
- `timestamp`: ISO 8601

### 4. Conformance Stamping

Validation reports are not phase output canonical artifacts. No `schema_id` or `artifact_status` applies.

### 5. Write Sequence

- Step 5.1: Write the traceability report to `docs/tier4_orchestration_state/validation_reports/<report_id>.json`

## Constitutional Constraint Enforcement

*Step 6 implementation — skill plan §4.6 and §7 Step 6. Each constraint from `skill_catalog.yaml` is mapped to a specific decision point in the execution logic and enforced as a hard failure. Cross-checked against CLAUDE.md §13.*

---

### Constraint 1: "Unattributed claims must be flagged, not silently accepted as Confirmed"

**Decision point in execution logic:** Step 2.3.3 — at the point each material claim's status is assigned based on traceability_footer examination.

**Exact failure condition:** A material claim has no matching source reference in `traceability_footer.primary_sources[]` AND the claim is about a project fact (partner capability, specific objective, specific outcome, specific metric) — AND the claim is assigned status "Confirmed" or "Inferred" rather than "Unresolved".

**Enforcement mechanism:** In Step 2.3.3, the status assignment rules are deterministic:
- **Unresolved** is mandatory when: no source reference is provided AND the claim is about a project fact. There is no judgment threshold — absence of source reference for a project-fact claim always yields Unresolved, not Confirmed.
- **Assumed** is the weakest permissible non-flagged status, applicable only to generic structural statements that no source needs to validate. Project-fact claims cannot be Assumed — they must be Unresolved.

If any material claim about a project fact is assigned status "Confirmed" or "Inferred" without a verifiable source reference in `primary_sources[]`: return SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="CONSTITUTIONAL_HALT", failure_reason="Material claim about project fact <claim_id> was assigned Confirmed/Inferred status without a Tier 1–4 source reference; unattributed project-fact claims must be flagged as Unresolved per CLAUDE.md §10.5 and §12.2"). No validation report written.

**Failure output:** SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="CONSTITUTIONAL_HALT"). No report written.

**Hard failure confirmation:** Yes — silently accepting unattributed project-fact claims as Confirmed is a categorical prohibition.

**CLAUDE.md §13 cross-reference:** §10.5 — "Unattributed claims must be flagged, not asserted." §12.2 — "Confirmed — directly evidenced by a named source in Tier 1–3; the source artifact must be named." §13.10 — "Producing outputs in Tier 5 that are not traceable to specific inputs in Tier 1–4."

---

### Constraint 2: "Confirmed status requires naming the specific source artifact"

**Decision point in execution logic:** Step 2.3.3 — at the point a claim is assigned status "Confirmed", and Step 3 — at the point the `claim_audit_results` array is constructed.

**Exact failure condition:** Any claim_audit_result entry has `status: "confirmed"` AND the `source_ref` field is empty, null, or contains only a directory path without a specific filename and relevant field identification. Equivalently: Confirmed status is assigned without naming the exact file in the Tier 1–4 hierarchy that supports the claim.

**Enforcement mechanism:** In Step 2.3.3, condition for Confirmed status requires both: (a) a `primary_sources[]` entry with a `source_path` referencing a specific Tier 1–4 file (not just a directory), AND (b) the content of that file being directly consistent with the claim.

DETERMINISTIC CHECK AT WRITE TIME:
IF `status == "confirmed"` AND `source_ref` is null, empty, OR is only a directory path (does not end in a filename with extension):
→ CONSTITUTIONAL_HALT immediately before writing the report
→ return SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="CONSTITUTIONAL_HALT", failure_reason="Claim <claim_id> assigned Confirmed status but source_ref does not name a specific artifact; CLAUDE.md §12.2 requires naming the specific source artifact for Confirmed status")
→ No report written

**Failure output:** SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="CONSTITUTIONAL_HALT"). No validation report written.

**Hard failure confirmation:** Yes — Confirmed status without a specific named source artifact is a constitutional violation per CLAUDE.md §12.2.

**CLAUDE.md §13 cross-reference:** §12.2 — "Confirmed — directly evidenced by a named source in Tier 1–3; the source artifact must be named." §10.5 — "Unattributed claims must be flagged, not asserted."

<!-- Step 6 complete: constitutional constraint enforcement implemented -->

## Failure Protocol

*Step 7 implementation — skill plan §4.8 and §7 Step 7. All five failure categories are handled. For every failure: SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category=<category>, failure_reason=<non-null string>). No artifact is written to a canonical output path when a failure is declared.*

---

### MISSING_INPUT

**Trigger conditions in this skill:**
- Step 1.1: `artifact_path` is absent or empty in `caller_context` → `failure_reason="artifact_path required in caller_context — the agent runtime must inject it"`
- Step 1.2 (section mode): Section file at `artifact_path` does not exist → `failure_reason="Proposal section file <artifact_path> not found"`
- Step 1.3 (assembled mode): `part_b_assembled_draft.json` is absent or schema mismatch → `failure_reason="part_b_assembled_draft.json not found or schema mismatch"`
- Step 1.5: No Tier 1–4 reference directory is accessible → `failure_reason="No Tier 1–4 reference artifacts accessible for traceability verification"`

**Required response:** `SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="MISSING_INPUT", failure_reason=<specific reason>)`

**Artifact write behavior:** No artifact written to any canonical output path. Skill halts immediately.

---

### MALFORMED_ARTIFACT

**Trigger conditions in this skill:**
- Step 1.4: A section file to be audited has `schema_id` not in the accepted set ("orch.tier5.proposal_section.v1", "orch.tier5.excellence_section.v1", "orch.tier5.impact_section.v1", "orch.tier5.implementation_section.v1") → recorded as a traceability failure for that section; evaluation continues. This does not produce a MALFORMED_ARTIFACT SkillResult halt — the schema mismatch is treated as a finding.

Note: schema mismatch in section files is surfaced as a traceability finding in the report, not as a MALFORMED_ARTIFACT halt.

**Artifact write behavior:** Not applicable (schema mismatch produces a finding in the report, not a halt).

---

### CONSTRAINT_VIOLATION

**Trigger conditions in this skill:**
No CONSTRAINT_VIOLATION conditions are defined for this skill; all constitutional constraint failures use CONSTITUTIONAL_HALT as appropriate.

**Artifact write behavior:** Not applicable.

---

### INCOMPLETE_OUTPUT

**Trigger conditions in this skill:**
No INCOMPLETE_OUTPUT conditions are explicitly defined in the execution logic. Write errors at Step 5.1 should return `failure_reason="Traceability report could not be written to validation_reports/"`.

**Required response:** `SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="INCOMPLETE_OUTPUT", failure_reason=<specific reason>)`

**Artifact write behavior:** No partial write to any canonical output path. Skill halts before writing.

---

### CONSTITUTIONAL_HALT

**Trigger conditions in this skill:**
- Constraint 1 (unattributed claims flagged, not silently accepted as Confirmed): Any material claim about a project fact is assigned status "Confirmed" or "Inferred" without a verifiable source reference in `traceability_footer.primary_sources[]` → `failure_reason="Material claim about project fact <claim_id> was assigned Confirmed/Inferred status without a Tier 1–4 source reference; unattributed project-fact claims must be flagged as Unresolved per CLAUDE.md §10.5 and §12.2"`
- Constraint 2 (Confirmed status requires naming the specific source artifact): Any claim_audit_result entry has `status: "confirmed"` AND `source_ref` is null, empty, or is only a directory path → `failure_reason="Claim <claim_id> assigned Confirmed status but source_ref does not name a specific artifact; CLAUDE.md §12.2 requires naming the specific source artifact for Confirmed status"`

**Required response:** `SkillResult(status="failure", failure_category="CONSTITUTIONAL_HALT", failure_reason=<specific reason>)`

**Artifact write behavior:** Immediate halt. No validation report written. A validation report entry MAY be written to `docs/tier4_orchestration_state/validation_reports/` documenting the halt if the directory is accessible, as `validation_reports/` is in this skill's declared `writes_to` scope.

---

### Universal Failure Rules

1. Every failure returns `SkillResult(status="failure")` with a non-null `failure_reason` string.
2. No canonical output artifact is written (partially or fully) when any failure category fires.
3. Exceptions: this skill's `writes_to` includes `docs/tier4_orchestration_state/validation_reports/`; a failure record MAY be written there even when the primary output fails.
4. The invoking agent receives the `SkillResult` and is responsible for logging the failure and halting phase execution per its own failure protocol.
5. Failure is a correct and valid output. Fabricated completion is a constitutional violation per CLAUDE.md §15.

<!-- Step 7 complete: failure protocol implemented -->

## Schema Validation

*Step 8 implementation — skill plan §7 Step 8. Group C skill whose sole output is a validation report file; no canonical `schema_id` applies. Conformance is governed by CLAUDE.md §10.5, §12.1, §12.2, §13.10.*

---

### Upstream input schema verification

- **Proposal section files** (`orch.tier5.proposal_section.v1`, `orch.tier5.excellence_section.v1`, `orch.tier5.impact_section.v1`, `orch.tier5.implementation_section.v1`): skill reads `content` or `sub_sections[].content`, `validation_status.claim_statuses[]`, `traceability_footer.primary_sources[]`. For criterion-aligned sections, `sub_sections[].content` is concatenated to form the auditable text. All field paths match their respective spec entries. The spec defines `validation_status.claim_statuses[].status` enum as lowercase `[confirmed, inferred, assumed, unresolved]` — the skill uses the same lowercase vocabulary. Compliant.
- **`part_b_assembled_draft.json`** (`orch.tier5.part_b_assembled_draft.v1`): skill reads `sections[].section_id, artifact_path`. Field paths match spec §2.1e. Compliant.
- **Tier 1–4 reference directories**: skill declares all four `extracted/` and Tier 3 directories in `reads_from`; checks only path existence and content consistency for traceability verification. No schema_id binding required for reference reads.

### Artifact: `traceability_<section_id>_<timestamp>.json` (validation report)

**Canonical schema:** None — operational validation report, not registered.

**Output Construction fields verification:**
| Field | Set by skill? | Governance | Conformant? |
|-------|---------------|------------|-------------|
| `report_id` | Yes (Step 3) | skill-defined | Yes |
| `skill_id` | Yes | matches frontmatter | Yes |
| `invoking_agent` | Yes | agent context | Yes |
| `run_id_reference` | Yes | agent context | Yes |
| `section_id_audited` | Yes | `section_id` or "all_sections" | Yes |
| `claim_audit_results[]` | Yes (Step 2.5, Step 3) | per entry: claim_id, claim_summary, status (enum: confirmed/inferred/assumed/unresolved), source_ref, flag_reason | Yes — status enum matches §12.2 vocabulary exactly |
| `summary` | Yes (Step 2.6, Step 3) | total_claims, confirmed, inferred, assumed, unresolved | Yes |
| `no_unsupported_claims_declaration` | Yes (Step 2.4) | boolean — matches spec's `traceability_footer.no_unsupported_claims_declaration` semantics | Yes |
| `timestamp` | Yes | ISO 8601 | Yes |

**CLAUDE.md §12.2 vocabulary compliance:** This skill's `claim_audit_results[].status` field uses lowercase `{confirmed, inferred, assumed, unresolved}` — directly aligned with the CLAUDE.md §12.2 validation status vocabulary and consistent with the upstream `proposal_section.v1` schema's `validation_status.claim_statuses[].status` enum. Constraint 1 and Constraint 2 enforce the §12.2 semantics: Confirmed requires named source; Unresolved is mandatory for unattributed project-fact claims; Assumed is restricted to generic structural statements. Full vocabulary conformance.

**`schema_id` / `artifact_status`:** Step 4 correctly states these do not apply to validation reports.

**reads_from compliance:** All six declared reference directories are used in the execution logic (Step 1.5, Step 2.3). Compliant.

**writes_to compliance:** Writes only to `docs/tier4_orchestration_state/validation_reports/`. Compliant.

**Gaps identified:** None.

**Corrections applied:** None.

# Canonical Inputs

## docs/tier2a_instrument_schemas/extracted/evaluator_expectation_registry.json

```json
{
  "instruments": [
    {
      "instrument_type": "RIA",
      "criteria": [
        {
          "criterion_id": "Excellence",
          "criterion_name": "Excellence",
          "threshold_score": 3,
          "evaluator_expectations": [
            "Clarity and pertinence of the project's objectives, and the extent to which the proposed work is ambitious, and goes beyond the state of the art.",
            "Soundness of the proposed methodology, including the underlying concepts, models, assumptions, inter-disciplinary approaches, appropriate consideration of the gender dimension in research and innovation content, and the quality of open science practices, including sharing and management of research outputs and engagement of citizens, civil society and end users where appropriate."
          ]
        },
        {
          "criterion_id": "Impact",
          "criterion_name": "Impact",
          "threshold_score": 3,
          "evaluator_expectations": [
            "Credibility of the pathways to achieve the expected outcomes and impacts specified in the work programme.",
            "Suitability and quality of the measures to maximise expected outcomes and impacts, as set out in the dissemination and exploitation plan, including communication activities."
          ]
        },
        {
          "criterion_id": "Quality and efficiency of the implementation",
          "criterion_name": "Quality and efficiency of the implementation",
          "threshold_score": 3,
          "evaluator_expectations": [
            "Quality and effectiveness of the work plan, assessment of risks, and appropriateness of the effort assigned to work packages, and the resources overall.",
            "Capacity and role of each participant, and the extent to which the consortium as a whole brings together the necessary expertise."
          ]
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}
```

## docs/tier2a_instrument_schemas/extracted/section_schema_registry.json

```json
{
  "instruments": [
    {
      "instrument_type": "RIA",
      "evaluation_form_ref": "ef_he-ria-ia_en.pdf",
      "evaluation_form_ref_assumption_note": "Assumed from application form filename naming convention (af_\u2192ef_); evaluation_forms/ directory not in declared inputs for this skill invocation. Must be verified against actual evaluation_forms/ directory contents.",
      "max_work_packages": null,
      "max_work_packages_note": "No maximum work package count stated in form. Form states: 'the number of work packages should be proportionate to the scale and complexity of the project.' Source: af_he-ria-ia_en.pdf Part B p.13 of 23.",
      "source_document": "af_he-ria-ia_en.pdf",
      "extracted_at": "2026-04-22T00:00:00Z",
      "project_duration_months": null,
      "project_duration_months_note": "Not specified in application form template; varies by call. Duration field in Part A Section 1 is entered by applicant. Source: af_he-ria-ia_en.pdf Part A p.4 of 24.",
      "max_deliverable_count": null,
      "max_deliverable_count_note": "No maximum deliverable count stated in form. Table 3.1c instruction states: 'Only include deliverables that you consider essential for effective project monitoring.' Source: af_he-ria-ia_en.pdf Part B p.17 of 23.",
      "part_b_page_limit_hard": 40,
      "part_b_page_limit_hard_note": "Directly stated in form: 'The title, list of participants and sections 1, 2 and 3, together, should not be longer than 40 pages.     "self_assessment_statement": "Ethics self-assessment is mandatory for all Horizon Europe proposals. This obligation is grounded in Tier 1 implementation_constraints.json (ethics_self_assessment_required: 'Applicants must complete an ethics self-assessment as part of the application; projects with ethics issues may undergo ethics review and ethics requirements may become contractual obligations'; source: wp-15-general-annexes_horizon-2026-2027_en.pdf p.16; programme-guide_horizon_en.pdf pp.25-28). The ethics self-assessment must be completed as part of Part A Section 4 (Ethics and Security) of the application form (docs/tier2a_instrument_schemas/extracted/section_schema_registry.json section A.4: 'This table should be completed as an essential part of your proposal').\n\nThree ethics categories are triggered by the MAESTRO project:\n\n(1) Category 8 \u2014 Artificial Intelligence: MAESTRO develops and deploys AI-based autonomous agent systems powered by large language models (WP2 planning engine; WP4 multi-agent coordination) validated in safety-relevant domains (WP5 clinical decision support; WP6 manufacturing). Ethical concerns related to human rights and values arising from autonomous AI decision-making must be addressed in the full ethics self-assessment. Ethics oversight is the responsibility of ATU (Ethics Compliance Coordinator, MGR-011, grounded in WP1 T1-03 and roles.json) with healthcare-specific oversight by NIHS (Healthcare Ethics Oversight Officer, MGR-012, grounded in roles.json key_responsibilities).\n\n(2) Category 4 \u2014 Personal Data (Special Category: Health Data): WP5 processes de-identified clinical datasets provided by NIHS (docs/tier3_project_instantiation/consortium/partners.json). De-identified health data constitutes special category personal data. The full ethics self-assessment must address lawful basis for processing, data minimisation, retention, and re-identification risk. Healthcare data governance is overseen by the Ethics and Quality Oversight Committee (ATU and NIHS).\n\n(3) Category 2 \u2014 Human Participants (medical context): WP5 T5-03 clinical expert validation may involve human participants in a medical study context. The full ethics self-assessment must clarify participant status, consent requirements, and applicability of EU Regulation 536/2014.\n\nCivil focus: The project addresses exclusively civil application domains (healthcare, manufacturing, logistics). No military applications are present in Tier 3 source documents. Civil focus compliance is consistent with Tier 1 civil_focus_constraint (implementation_constraints.json; source: wp-15-general-annexes_horizon-2026-2027_en.pdf pp.14-17).\n\nGender dimension in research and innovation content: Integration of the gender dimension into research and innovation content follows the Tier 1 default rule that it is mandatory unless the topic explicitly states non-relevance (implementation_constraints.json: gender_dimension_in_content; source: programme-guide_horizon_en.pdf pp.17-20; wp-15-general-annexes_horizon-2026-2027_en.pdf p.24; ef_he-ria-ia_en.pdf pp.4-5). No Tier 2B exemption source is currently cited in this Phase 6 artifact; Phase 8 drafting must either add the relevant Tier 2B topic-source reference (from docs/tier2b_topic_and_call_sources/extracted/) confirming whether the topic text states non-relevance, or keep the claim framed as pending call-specific confirmation. The gender dimension analysis must be addressed in section B.1.2 (Methodology) of the application form.\n\nGender equality plans (GEPs): The Tier 3 compliance_profile.json records gender_plan_required: true as a compliance flag derived during call binding. This is consistent with the Tier 1 programme-level rule (implementation_constraints.json: gender_equality_plan_eligibility: 'Public bodies, research organisations and higher education establishments in Member States/Associated Countries must have a gender equality plan at grant signature and during the grant'; source: wp-15-general-annexes_horizon-2026-2027_en.pdf pp.18-19; programme-guide_horizon_en.pdf pp.16-17). No Tier 2B extracted source path in scope_requirements.json or call_constraints.json cites GEP requirement as a topic-specific mandate beyond the general Tier 1 programme obligation. Partners ATU (DE, HES), CERIA (FR, REC), BIIS (NL, HES), ISIA (IT, HES), NIHS (SE, HES), and FIIT (ES, REC) must have GEPs at grant signature per Tier 1 rule. This is confirmed as an eligibility criterion in application form section A.2 (docs/tier2a_instrument_schemas/extracted/section_schema_registry.json).\n\nGender balance in management: Beneficiaries must promote equal opportunities and aim for gender balance at all management levels per Tier 1 (implementation_constraints.json: gender_management_balance_guidance; source: wp-15-general-annexes_horizon-2026-2027_en.pdf p.18). Implementation through recruitment and appointment practices across the consortium management roles defined in this artifact.\n\nOpen science and AI-on-demand platform: Communicable results must be shared with the European R&D community through the AI-on-demand platform. This is confirmed as a Tier 2B mandate (docs/tier2b_topic_and_call_sources/extracted/scope_requirements.json SR-10: 'Communicable results must be shared with the European R&D community through the AI-on-demand platform', source_section: platform_requirements; docs/tier2b_topic_and_call_sources/extracted/call_constraints.json CC-05: same requirement, source_section: call_entry.scope). {
```
```json
  "schema_id": "orch.tier5.implementation_section.v1",

  "criterion": "Quality and efficiency of the implementation",
  "sub_sections": [
    {
      "sub_section_id": "B.3.1",
      "title": "Work plan and resources",
      "content": "OVERALL WORK PLAN STRUCTURE\n\nMAESTRO organises its 48-month research programme into nine work packages (WP1\u2013WP9) structured across four functional layers proportionate to the scale and complexity of an 8-partner RIA addressing three research pillars and three demonstrator domains. The management layer (WP1, lead ATU) provides consortium governance, quality assurance, and ethics compliance \u2014 including mandatory cohesion activities with ADRA and the GenAI4EU central Hub (SR-09; CC-03/CC-04) \u2014 throughout the project. The research pillar layer (WP2\u2013WP4) develops the three foundational MAESTRO capabilities in parallel: neuro-symbolic planning and reasoning (WP2, lead ATU), adaptive memory architecture (WP3, lead BIIS), and decentralised multi-agent coordination (WP4, lead CERIA). The application and validation layer (WP5\u2013WP7) validates the integrated MAESTRO framework in three real-world application domains: healthcare clinical decision support (WP5, lead NIHS), manufacturing process optimisation (WP6, lead ISIA), and logistics supply chain operations (WP7, lead ELI), satisfying the Apply AI sector requirement of SR-07. The horizontal layer (WP8\u2013WP9) integrates the research pillars, manages cross-demonstrator evaluation and benchmarking aligned with SR-06/CC-06 (WP8, lead FIIT), and executes dissemination, exploitation, and AI-on-demand platform contributions required under SR-10 and CC-05 (WP9, lead BAL).\n\nTABLE 3.1a \u2014 LIST OF WORK PACKAGES\n\nWP1: Project Management and Coordination | Lead: ATU | M1\u2013M48\nWP2: Neuro-Symbolic Planning and Reasoning Engine | Lead: ATU | M1\u2013M36\nWP3: Adaptive Memory Architecture | Lead: BIIS | M1\u2013M30\nWP4: Decentralised Multi-Agent Coordination | Lead: CERIA | M3\u2013M36\nWP5: Healthcare Demonstrator \u2014 Clinical Decision Support | Lead: NIHS | M12\u2013M42\nWP6: Manufacturing Demonstrator \u2014 Process Optimisation | Lead: ISIA | M12\u2013M42\nWP7: Logistics Transfer Demonstrator \u2014 Cross-Sector Generalisation | Lead: ELI | M12\u2013M42\nWP8: Integration, Evaluation and Benchmarking | Lead: FIIT | M6\u2013M48\nWP9: Dissemination, Exploitation and Communication | Lead: BAL | M1\u2013M48\n\nPerson-month allocations per WP and partner are confirmed as structurally consistent in the validated budget response (budget gate assessment: pass; validation ref: budget_validation_response_2026-04-24T14:30:00Z.json). Specific figures are drawn exclusively from that validated response.\n\nTABLE 3.1b \u2014 WORK PACKAGE DESCRIPTIONS\n\nWP1 (Lead: ATU; contributing: CERIA, BIIS, ISIA, NIHS, ELI, BAL, FIIT; M1\u2013M48). Objectives: (1) Ensure effective consortium governance, administrative management, and reporting. (2) Maintain quality assurance, risk management, and ethics compliance across all project activities. Tasks: T1-01 Consortium governance and financial management (M1\u2013M48, ATU) \u2014 covers financial management, grant agreement compliance, EC/ADRA liaison, and GenAI4EU Hub cohesion per CC-03/CC-04; T1-02 Quality assurance and risk monitoring (M1\u2013M48, ATU) \u2014 manages the risk register and milestone reviews; T1-03 Ethics compliance oversight and coordination with GenAI4EU Hub (M1\u2013M48, ATU) \u2014 oversees ethics self-assessment categories 2, 4, and 8 and satisfies mandatory cohesion requirement of SR-09.\n\nWP2 (Lead: ATU; contributing: CERIA, BIIS, BAL; M1\u2013M36). Objectives: (1) Design and implement a hybrid neuro-symbolic planning engine with formal sub-task graph decomposition. (2) Integrate MCTS and HTN planning with LLM-based heuristics and verifiable plan self-correction. Addresses SR-02 (robust planning and reasoning) and SR-01 (next-generation AI agents). Tasks: T2-01 Sub-task graph decomposition design with formal pre/post-conditions (M1\u2013M12, ATU) \u2014 establishes the formal planning substrate; T2-02 MCTS and HTN planning integration with LLM heuristics (M6\u2013M24, ATU) \u2014 integrates neural and symbolic planning methods; T2-03 Plan monitoring and self-correction implementation (M18\u2013M36, ATU) \u2014 completes the engine with verifiable self-correction. WP2 outputs feed directly into WP5, WP6, WP7 (planning capability for demonstrators) and WP8 (unified framework integration).\n\nWP3 (Lead: BIIS; contributing: ATU, CERIA, BAL; M1\u2013M30). Objectives: (1) Design and implement a unified tri-store memory architecture with a learned memory controller. (2) Develop memory indexing, retrieval, and forgetting mechanisms for long-horizon agent interactions. Addresses SR-03 (effective memory and state management). Tasks: T3-01 Tri-store memory architecture design (M1\u2013M12, BIIS) \u2014 establishes working, episodic, and semantic memory stores; T3-02 Memory indexing and retrieval strategy implementation (M6\u2013M24, BIIS) \u2014 enables efficient retrieval across long-horizon interactions; T3-03 Forgetting mechanism and coherence maintenance (M18\u2013M30, BIIS) \u2014 ensures temporal coherence. WP3 outputs feed into WP5, WP6, WP7, and WP8.\n\nWP4 (Lead: CERIA; contributing: ATU, BIIS; M3\u2013M36). Objectives: (1) Develop formally specified task-delegation and negotiation protocols for heterogeneous AI agents. (2) Demonstrate convergence guarantees and auditable multi-agent interaction with shared tool access governance. Tasks: T4-01 Task-delegation and negotiation protocol design (M3\u2013M15, CERIA) \u2014 produces the formal protocol specification with convergence properties; T4-02 Convergence and conflict resolution under partial observability (M12\u2013M24, CERIA) \u2014 addresses real-world coordination challenges; T4-03 Auditable multi-agent interaction trace module (M18\u2013M36, CERIA) \u2014 enables verifiable multi-agent behaviour logging. WP4 outputs feed into WP5, WP6, WP7, and WP8.\n\nWP5 (Lead: NIHS; contributing: ATU, BIIS, BAL, FIIT; M12\u2013M42). Objectives: (1) Validate the MAESTRO framework in a clinical decision support use case with HL7 FHIR integration. (2) Conduct clinical expert validation of specialist sub-agents against diagnostic benchmarks. Addresses SR-07 (healthcare Apply AI sector). Depends on WP2 (planning engine), WP3 (memory system), and WP4 (coordination protocols). Tasks: T5-01 Clinical use case definition and diagnostic benchmark design (M12\u2013M18, NIHS) \u2014 defines clinical scope and secures ethics approvals and data access for de-identified clinical datasets; T5-02 HL7 FHIR integration and specialist sub-agent deployment (M18\u2013M36, NIHS) \u2014 deploys MAESTRO with clinical data adapters; T5-03 Clinical expert validation and results analysis (M36\u2013M42, NIHS) \u2014 validates across 500 clinical cases. WP5 outputs feed into WP8 cross-demonstrator evaluation.\n\nWP6 (Lead: ISIA; contributing: ATU, CERIA, BAL, FIIT; M12\u2013M42). Objectives: (1) Validate the MAESTRO framework for manufacturing process optimisation in a pilot factory setting. (2) Demonstrate multi-agent real-time coordination across production segments against defined KPIs. Addresses SR-07 (advanced manufacturing Apply AI sector). Depends on WP2, WP3, WP4. Tasks: T6-01 Production scenario definition and KPI framework design (M12\u2013M18, ISIA); T6-02 Digital twin integration and multi-agent coordination deployment (M18\u2013M36, ISIA) \u2014 results validated in Testing and Experiment Facilities per CC-07; T6-03 Pilot factory operational validation (M36\u2013M42, ISIA) \u2014 three-month operational validation period. WP6 outputs feed into WP8.\n\nWP7 (Lead: ELI; contributing: CERIA, BAL, FIIT; M12\u2013M42). Objectives: (1) Validate MAESTRO generalisation in logistics and supply chain operations across three international corridors. (2) Confirm integrated architecture transferability beyond primary call sectors using real operational data. Depends on WP2, WP3, WP4. Tasks: T7-01 Logistics scenario and disruption recovery benchmark design (M12\u2013M24, ELI); T7-02 Agent-based planning and negotiation deployment across supply chain (M18\u2013M36, ELI); T7-03 Operational validation across three international corridors (M36\u2013M42, ELI). WP7 outputs feed into WP8.\n\nWP8 (Lead: FIIT; contributing: ATU, CERIA, BIIS, ISIA, NIHS, ELI, BAL; M6\u2013M48). Objectives: (1) Define a cross-cutting evaluation framework and integrate all MAESTRO research pillars into a unified system. (2) Produce a standardised benchmark suite for community adoption and cross-demonstrator evaluation. Addresses SR-06/CC-06 (KPIs, benchmarking, progress monitoring) and SR-11/CC-07 (AI Factories and Testing and Experiment Facilities linkage). Depends on WP5, WP6, WP7. Tasks: T8-01 Cross-cutting evaluation framework and KPI definition (M6\u2013M12, FIIT) \u2014 establishes shared evaluation metrics early so all pillar WPs are measured consistently; T8-02 MAESTRO unified framework integration (M18\u2013M42, FIIT) \u2014 integrates WP2, WP3, WP4 outputs into a deployable unified framework; T8-03 Cross-demonstrator benchmarking and community benchmark release (M42\u2013M48, FIIT). WP8 feeds into WP9.\n\nWP9 (Lead: BAL; contributing: ATU, ISIA, ELI, FIIT; M1\u2013M48). Objectives: (1) Manage open-source framework release, community building, and AI-on-demand platform contributions per SR-10/CC-05. (2) Develop and execute consortium exploitation strategy and lead public communication. Depends on WP8. Tasks: T9-03 Communication, website, and public engagement (M1\u2013M48, BAL) \u2014 runs continuously; T9-02 Exploitation strategy development and IP management (M3\u2013M36, BAL); T9-01 Open-source release management and community building (M18\u2013M48, BAL) \u2014 manages the open-source release and AI-on-demand platform contributions.\n\nTABLE 3.1c \u2014 LIST OF DELIVERABLES\n\nD1-01 Project management and quality plan (WP1, ATU, R, PU, M3); D1-02 Data management plan (WP1, ATU, R, PU, M6) \u2014 mandatory distinct deliverable within 6 months per application form; D2-01 Neuro-symbolic planning architecture specification (WP2, ATU, R, PU, M18); D2-02 Planning engine software prototype (WP2, ATU, OTHER, PU, M36); D3-01 Memory architecture design specification (WP3, BIIS, R, PU, M12); D3-02 Adaptive memory system software (WP3, BIIS, OTHER, PU, M30); D4-01 Multi-agent coordination protocol specification (WP4, CERIA, R, PU, M18); D4-02 Decentralised coordination software (WP4, CERIA, OTHER, PU, M36); D5-01 Clinical decision support use case specification (WP5, NIHS, R, SEN, M18); D5-02 Healthcare demonstrator evaluation dataset (WP5, NIHS, DATA, SEN, M42); D6-01 Manufacturing use case and KPI specification (WP6, ISIA, R, PU, M18); D6-02 Manufacturing process optimisation demonstrator software (WP6, ISIA, OTHER, PU, M42); D7-01 Logistics demonstrator specification and benchmark report (WP7, ELI, R, PU, M24); D7-02 Cross-sector generalisation evaluation dataset (WP7, ELI, DATA, PU, M42); D8-01 Evaluation framework and benchmark specification (WP8, FIIT, R, PU, M12); D8-02 MAESTRO benchmark suite dataset (WP8, FIIT, DATA, PU, M42); D8-03 Final integration and evaluation report (WP8, FIIT, R, PU, M48); D9-01 Dissemination and exploitation plan (WP9, BAL, R, PU, M6) \u2014 admissibility condition, mandatory distinct deliverable within 6 months; D9-02 Open-source software release (WP9, BAL, OTHER, PU, M36); D9-03 Final dissemination and impact report (WP9, BAL, R, PU, M48). Type codes: R=document/report; OTHER=software; DATA=data set. Dissemination levels: PU=public fully open; SEN=sensitive (applied to clinical data deliverables in WP5 reflecting GDPR obligations for special-category health data).\n\nTIMELINE AND GANTT CHART NARRATIVE\n\nThe 48-month timeline unfolds in four overlapping phases. Phase 1 (M1\u2013M12) establishes integration contracts and architecture specifications (MS1, M3), early research foundations across all three pillars, and demonstrator use case definitions (MS5, M12). Phase 2 (M12\u2013M24) completes pillar prototype development (MS2 planning engine v1.0, M12; MS3 memory architecture v1.0, M12; MS4 multi-agent protocol with convergence proofs, M15) and achieves Integrated MAESTRO Framework v1.0 with all three pillars and the tool orchestration layer operating together (MS6, M24). Phase 3 (M24\u2013M42) deploys the framework in all three demonstrator environments (MS7, M30), confirms research pillar quantitative targets (MS8, M36), and completes full cross-demonstrator validation (MS9, M42). Phase 4 (M42\u2013M48) delivers the community benchmark suite, open-source release and AI-on-demand platform publication (MS10, M45), and final project closure (MS11, M48). Management (WP1 T1-01/T1-02/T1-03) and communication (WP9 T9-03) tasks run continuously throughout M1\u2013M48.\n\nThe critical path runs through the neuro-symbolic planning pillar (T2-01 M1\u2013M12, T2-02 M6\u2013M24, T2-03 M18\u2013M36), through the healthcare demonstrator (T5-01 M12\u2013M18, T5-02 M18\u2013M36, T5-03 M36\u2013M42), and concludes with cross-demonstrator benchmarking (T8-03 M42\u2013M48). Nine structurally equivalent critical paths of equal length (three dependency edges) have been identified, reflecting the symmetric dependency structure: each of WP2, WP3, and WP4 feeds each of WP5, WP6, and WP7, which all feed WP8, which feeds WP9. Delay in any research pillar will therefore cascade to at least one demonstrator and to the integration timeline. The dependency graph is confirmed as a directed acyclic graph with no cycles (Kahn algorithm verified, 36 nodes processed).\n\nTABLE 3.1d \u2014 LIST OF MILESTONES\n\nMS1 (M3, WP1, ATU): Architecture specification and integration contracts finalised. Verification: shared data representations, API contracts, and integration interfaces for all three pillars reviewed and accepted by all pillar leads; tool registry schema and integration test harness operational.\nMS2 (M12, WP2, ATU): Planning engine v1.0 \u2014 baseline neuro-symbolic integration. Verification: decomposition of \u22655 benchmark task types with verifiable pre/post-conditions; measurable improvement over LLM-only baseline on \u22651 standardised agent benchmark.\nMS3 (M12, WP3, BIIS): Memory architecture v1.0 \u2014 tri-store prototype operational. Verification: all three memory stores individually operational; coherence improvement over context-window-only baseline on synthetic long-horizon tasks (>20 steps).\nMS4 (M15, WP4, CERIA): Multi-agent protocol specification with convergence proofs. Verification: formal protocol specification complete; convergence proofs for \u22653 core task classes; simulation validation with \u22655 heterogeneous agents.\nMS5 (M12, WP8, FIIT): Demonstrator use cases defined and domain data secured. Verification: clinical use cases, manufacturing scenarios, and logistics corridors fully specified with acceptance criteria; ethics approvals for clinical data granted; factory access agreement signed; logistics data access terms agreed.\nMS6 (M24, WP8, FIIT): Integrated MAESTRO framework v1.0 with tool orchestration layer. Verification: all three pillars and tool orchestration layer integrated; tool registry populated with \u226510 tools/APIs; end-to-end evaluation on cross-cutting benchmarks; framework deployable in all demonstrator environments.\nMS7 (M30, WP8, FIIT): Demonstrator v1.0 \u2014 initial deployment in all three demonstrator environments. Verification: MAESTRO deployed in healthcare, manufacturing, and logistics environments; domain-specific adapters operational; initial functional evaluation completed in each sector.\nMS8 (M36, WP2, ATU): Research pillar targets achieved. Verification: \u226540% plan success improvement (OBJ-1); \u226530% memory coherence improvement (OBJ-2); \u226525% joint task completion improvement (OBJ-3); all results reproducible and documented.\nMS9 (M42, WP8, FIIT): Demonstrator validation complete \u2014 all environments. Verification: healthcare validated on 500 clinical cases (OBJ-4); manufacturing validated over 3-month operational period (OBJ-5); logistics validated across 3 corridors (OBJ-6); tool orchestration validated with \u226530 tools/APIs registered (OBJ-8); cross-demonstrator evaluation report completed; architectural transferability to in-vehicle autonomous driving mapped.\nMS10 (M45, WP9, BAL): Open-source release and platform contributions delivered. Verification: MAESTRO framework released as open-source on GitHub; benchmark suite published on AI-on-demand platform (SR-10, CC-05); documentation and tutorials available; EDIH dissemination initiated in \u22653 hubs.\nMS11 (M48, WP1, ATU): Project completion and final review. Verification: all deliverables submitted; final exploitation plans per partner delivered; TEF validation reports completed; final review documentation compiled.\n\nTABLE 3.1e \u2014 CRITICAL RISKS FOR IMPLEMENTATION\n\nEvaluators assess risk management as part of the Quality and efficiency criterion. The MAESTRO risk register identifies eleven implementation risks across technical, regulatory, operational, and management categories. The highest-severity risks and their mitigations are:\n\nRISK-01 (WP2, technical, medium likelihood, high impact): Neuro-symbolic integration performance. Mitigation: modular architecture with well-defined symbolic/neural interfaces; LLM-only planner fallback modes for latency-critical scenarios; integration testing commencing M6 rather than M18. Contingency: deliver symbolic planning as a post-hoc verification layer if full co-generation is not achievable at TRL 5.\n\nRISK-04 (WP5, regulatory, medium likelihood, high impact): Clinical dataset access delayed or restricted by ethics review. Mitigation: ethics applications submitted in M1 (pre-project preparation initiated); publicly available clinical datasets (MIMIC-IV, eICU) as interim validation sources; data abstraction layer enabling seamless data source switching. Contingency: exclusively public clinical benchmarks with synthetic patient data if proprietary access is blocked.\n\nRISK-07 (WP2/WP3/WP4/WP8, technical, high likelihood, medium impact): Rapid LLM advancement changing baseline assumptions. Mitigation: model-agnostic interfaces across all MAESTRO components; annual baseline re-evaluation at M12, M24, M36. MAESTRO's value lies in the architecture (planning, memory, coordination) not in any specific LLM.\n\nRISK-09 (WP1, management, low likelihood, high impact): Partner withdrawal or key personnel departure. Mitigation: each pillar covered by \u22652 partners with relevant expertise; deputy PI appointments for each WP lead; consortium agreement commitment clauses and transition procedures.\n\nRISK-10 (WP2/WP3/WP4/WP8, technical, medium likelihood, high impact): Framework integration complexity across independently developed pillars. Mitigation: shared data representations, API contracts, and tool registry schemas defined in M1\u2013M3 (MS1, WP8 early deliverable); integration checkpoints every 6 months; BAL assigned as cross-pillar integration engineer. Contingency: composition-based approach (lightweight orchestration layer) if deep integration proves infeasible.\n\nRISK-11 (WP2/WP3/WP5/WP6/WP7/WP8, technical, medium likelihood, medium impact): External tool and API heterogeneity across three demonstrator domains (HL7 FHIR, OPC-UA, logistics APIs). Mitigation: minimal common adapter interface defined in M1\u2013M3; prioritisation of most critical APIs per demonstrator; reuse of existing open-source connector libraries. Full risk register with all eleven risks (RISK-01 through RISK-11) is held in the implementation architecture artifact (risk_register_ref).\n\nTABLES 3.1f\u20133.1h \u2014 STAFF EFFORT, SUBCONTRACTING, AND EQUIPMENT\n\nPerson-month allocations per participant per work package (Table 3.1f), subcontracting cost items (Table 3.1g), and major equipment purchase costs (Table 3.1h) are governed exclusively by the validated Lump Sum Budget Planner response. The budget gate assessment confirms structural consistency: all nine work packages (WP1\u2013WP9) and all eight consortium partners (ATU, CERIA, BIIS, ISIA, NIHS, ELI, BAL, FIIT) are confirmed present in the validated budget with no blocking inconsistencies. The effort distribution is consistent with WP lead responsibilities as documented in the work package structure and partner roles. No specific budget figures are introduced in this narrative; all cost data is drawn exclusively from the validated budget response held in the integration received directory.",

      "content": "CONSORTIUM COMPOSITION AND MATCH TO PROJECT OBJECTIVES\n\nThe MAESTRO consortium comprises eight organisations across six EU and associated countries, combining the full range of expertise and infrastructure required to develop, validate, and transfer next-generation AI agent capabilities to real-world application sectors. The consortium matches MAESTRO's objectives precisely: three research universities and institutes lead the three foundational research pillars (ATU, CERIA, BIIS); three domain organisations lead validation in the three Apply AI sectors (NIHS, ISIA, ELI); one private AI lab provides LLM engineering and open-source platform capacity across all work packages (BAL); and one applied research and technology centre provides evaluation rigour, benchmarking, and EDIH technology transfer capacity (FIIT). Each partner has a clearly defined, non-overlapping primary role and has demonstrated the capabilities and infrastructure necessary to fulfil it.\n\nATU \u2014 Alpenstadt Technical University (DE, HES; coordinator; WP1 and WP2 lead): ATU's Chair of AI Foundations has pioneered work in neuro-symbolic AI, automated planning, and LLM-based reasoning systems \u2014 precisely the expertise required to lead the neuro-symbolic planning pillar (WP2, addressing SR-02). As project coordinator, ATU provides consortium governance, financial management, EC and ADRA liaison (CC-03), and GenAI4EU Hub cohesion coordination (CC-04). ATU also contributes to WP3 (memory integration), WP4 (protocol design), WP5 (clinical demonstrator support), WP8 (unified framework integration), and WP9 (dissemination).\n\nCERIA \u2014 Centre Europ\u00e9en de Recherche en Informatique Avanc\u00e9e (FR, REC; WP4 lead): CERIA's multi-agent systems team has extensive expertise in formal coordination protocols, distributed AI, and game-theoretic multi-agent cooperation. This makes CERIA uniquely suited to lead WP4, which delivers the formally specified task-delegation and negotiation protocols with convergence guarantees that all three demonstrators depend upon. CERIA also contributes formal verification expertise to WP2 and WP3, and supports the logistics demonstrator coordination scenarios in WP7 and framework integration in WP8.\n\nBIIS \u2014 Breda Institute for Intelligent Systems (NL, HES; WP3 lead): BIIS is a pioneer in retrieval-augmented generation and memory-augmented neural networks, hosting leading research groups in deep learning and information retrieval. This expertise directly corresponds to the tri-store adaptive memory architecture objectives of WP3, which addresses SR-03. BIIS also contributes to WP2 (memory-planning integration), WP4 (memory-coordination interfaces), WP5 (clinical long-horizon interaction memory), and WP8.\n\nISIA \u2014 Istituto Superiore di Ingegneria Avanzata (IT, HES; WP6 lead): ISIA's AI for Manufacturing lab has extensive operational experience in digital twins, smart factory systems, and AI-driven process optimisation. This expertise is directly relevant to WP6, where ISIA provides the pilot factory environment and manufacturing domain knowledge for the advanced manufacturing demonstrator (SR-07). ISIA's digital twin infrastructure mitigates RISK-05 (factory access disruption) by enabling high-fidelity simulation during development phases. ISIA contributes to WP1, WP8, and WP9.\n\nNIHS \u2014 Nordic Institute of Health Sciences (SE, HES; WP5 lead): NIHS's Centre for Health Informatics conducts research on AI-assisted clinical decision support and clinical NLP, and provides access to de-identified clinical datasets and established clinical validation pathways. This healthcare-specific infrastructure and expertise is essential for WP5, the healthcare demonstrator (SR-07). NIHS also holds primary responsibility for ethics oversight of healthcare data handling, governing GDPR compliance for special-category health data (ETHICS-02) and Category 2 human participant considerations (ETHICS-03). NIHS contributes to WP1 and WP8.\n\nELI \u2014 EuroLog International AG (CH, PRC; WP7 lead): ELI is a major European logistics company operating in over 80 countries, with an Innovation Lab focused on AI-powered logistics optimisation and autonomous planning systems. ELI provides the unique combination of real-world logistics operations data and operational deployment environments across three international corridors required for the cross-sector transfer demonstrator (WP7). ELI's commercial role in MAESTRO ensures direct exploitation routes into logistics sector adoption and provides an industrial anchor for the framework's generalisation claim. ELI contributes to WP1, WP8, and WP9.\n\nBAL \u2014 Boreal AI Labs Oy (FI, PRC; WP9 lead): BAL is a leading European private AI lab specialising in building custom large language models, LLM fine-tuning, and production-grade AI deployment. BAL's expertise bridges the research and application layers of MAESTRO: BAL contributes LLM integration and deployment engineering to all six research and demonstrator WPs (WP2, WP3, WP4, WP5, WP6, WP7) and leads WP9, managing open-source release, AI-on-demand platform contributions (SR-10, CC-05), and consortium exploitation strategy. BAL's role as cross-pillar integration engineer (RISK-10 mitigation) is essential for the unified framework integration in WP8.\n\nFIIT \u2014 Fundaci\u00f3n Ib\u00e9rica de Innovaci\u00f3n Tecnol\u00f3gica (ES, REC; WP8 lead): FIIT's AI and Data Analytics division leads work on AI evaluation frameworks, benchmarking methodologies, and technology transfer through European Digital Innovation Hubs (EDIHs). FIIT is the evaluation and integration spine of MAESTRO, leading WP8 to define the cross-cutting evaluation framework and KPIs (SR-06, CC-06), integrate all research pillars into a unified deployable system, coordinate with AI Factories and Testing and Experiment Facilities (SR-11, CC-07), and drive EDIH network dissemination. FIIT contributes to WP5, WP6, WP7, and WP9.\n\nCOMPLEMENTARITY AND COVERAGE OF THE VALUE CHAIN\n\nThe consortium covers the full value chain from fundamental AI research through applied domain validation to industrial deployment and European community scaling. The three research pillar leads (ATU, CERIA, BIIS) together address all four research areas of SR-05: advanced self-planning and self-optimisation (WP2, ATU), memory-augmented agents for long-term reasoning (WP3, BIIS), advanced multi-agent frameworks for collaborative agents (WP4, CERIA), and external tool and API integration (SR-04) addressed across all pillar WPs. The three demonstrator leads (NIHS, ISIA, ELI) cover the three Apply AI sectors explicitly identified in SR-07 and CC-10: healthcare, advanced manufacturing, and logistics (providing cross-sector transfer evidence for the in-vehicle autonomous driving sector). BAL bridges the research and deployment layers; FIIT bridges the research and policy/industry transfer layers. No partner duplicates another's primary competence. Each partner is both necessary for and sufficient within its primary role.\n\nACCESS TO CRITICAL INFRASTRUCTURE\n\nNIHS provides de-identified clinical datasets and established clinical validation pathways for WP5 healthcare demonstrator development and validation. ISIA provides a pilot factory environment with digital twin infrastructure for WP6 manufacturing demonstrator deployment. ELI provides real-world logistics operational data and multi-corridor deployment environments for WP7 cross-sector transfer validation. ATU, CERIA, and BIIS bring research computing infrastructure for algorithmic development and training. FIIT connects MAESTRO to AI-on-demand platform infrastructure (CC-05, SR-10) and EDIH networks for technology transfer (CC-07, SR-11).\n\nGENDER EQUALITY PLANS\n\nPartners ATU (DE, HES), CERIA (FR, REC), BIIS (NL, HES), ISIA (IT, HES), NIHS (SE, HES), and FIIT (ES, REC) are public bodies, higher education establishments, or research organisations from EU Member States and are required to hold Gender Equality Plans at the time of grant signature, in compliance with the eligibility criterion in application form Section A.2.",
```

```json
    {
      "sub_section_id": "B.1.1",
      "title": "Objectives and ambition",
      "content": "MAESTRO (Multi-Agent Ecosystem for Strategic Task Reasoning and Orchestration) addresses the foundational scientific and technological challenge of building next-generation AI agent architectures that are robust, trustworthy, and deployable in real-world settings. The project is directly aligned with topic HORIZON-CL4-2026-05-DIGITAL-EMERGING-02, targeting both expected outcomes: significant improvements in the autonomy, robustness and reliability of AI agents through advanced planning mechanisms, memory management, and reasoning capabilities (EO-01); and innovative multi-agent frameworks demonstrating effective decentralised coordination and collaboration among multiple AI agents beyond the capabilities of individual agents (EO-02). MAESTRO is further directly responsive to the mandatory scope requirements of the topic: research on next-generation AI agents powered by large language models (SR-01); robust planning, reasoning, and search mechanisms (SR-02); effective memory and state management (SR-03); integration of external tools and APIs as an essential architectural element (SR-04); coverage of at least one research area from the designated list (SR-05, satisfied across three of four areas); and demonstration in at least one Apply AI sector (SR-07, satisfied across two sectors plus a transfer demonstrator).\n\nPROJECT OBJECTIVES\n\nMAESTRO pursues eight interconnected objectives across a 48-month programme, each with defined measurable performance targets, identified responsible partners, and scheduled target months:\n\nOBJ-1 \u2014 Neuro-Symbolic Planning Engine (ATU lead, Month 36): Develop a hybrid neuro-symbolic planning engine that decomposes high-level natural language goals into executable sub-task graphs with formally specified pre-conditions, post-conditions, and verification checkpoints, integrating Monte Carlo Tree Search (MCTS) and hierarchical task networks (HTN) with LLM-driven heuristic evaluation and plan monitoring with self-correction. Measurable target: \u226540% improvement in plan success rate over pure LLM-based baselines (ReAct, Reflexion) on standardised agent benchmarks (WebArena, SWE-bench, GAIA) for tasks requiring more than 10 sequential steps.\n\nOBJ-2 \u2014 Unified Adaptive Memory Architecture (BIIS lead, Month 30): Design and implement a unified three-store memory architecture \u2014 working memory, episodic memory, and semantic memory \u2014 with a learned memory controller that manages information flow between stores, balancing recall accuracy against computational cost. Measurable target: \u226530% improvement in task coherence and factual consistency over context-window-only baselines in interaction sequences exceeding 50 agent steps on MAESTRO's long-horizon evaluation suite.\n\nOBJ-3 \u2014 Decentralised Multi-Agent Coordination Protocols (CERIA lead, Month 36): Develop formally specified task-delegation and negotiation protocols enabling heterogeneous AI agents to coordinate on shared objectives with provable convergence guarantees and auditable interaction traces. Measurable target: effective coordination of \u22655 heterogeneous agents on shared tasks, \u226525% improvement in joint task completion over independent agent baselines, and formal proof of protocol convergence.\n\nOBJ-4 \u2014 Healthcare Demonstrator \u2014 Clinical Decision Support (NIHS lead, Month 42): Validate the integrated MAESTRO framework in a clinical decision support system that assists clinicians in diagnostic reasoning by autonomously gathering patient data, planning differential diagnoses, and coordinating specialist sub-agents across five diagnostic domains. Measurable target: diagnostic reasoning accuracy within 10% of specialist clinician performance on a benchmark of 500 de-identified clinical cases, validated by clinical experts at NIHS.\n\nOBJ-5 \u2014 Manufacturing Demonstrator \u2014 Process Optimisation (ISIA lead, Month 42): Validate the integrated MAESTRO framework in a multi-agent system that monitors, diagnoses, and optimises manufacturing processes in real time across production line segments. Measurable target: \u226515% reduction in defect rates and \u226510% reduction in energy consumption compared to baseline operations in a pilot factory environment at ISIA, validated over a three-month operational period.\n\nOBJ-6 \u2014 Logistics Transfer Demonstrator \u2014 Cross-Sector Generalisation (ELI lead, Month 42): Validate the generalisability and portability of the integrated MAESTRO architecture through a logistics and supply chain demonstrator coordinating operations across multiple actors and re-planning in response to disruptions. Measurable target: \u226520% improvement in disruption recovery time and \u226515% improvement in delivery schedule adherence on ELI operational scenarios across three supply chain corridors.\n\nOBJ-7 \u2014 Open Framework Release and Ecosystem Contribution (BAL lead, Month 48): Release the MAESTRO agent framework as open-source software, contribute all models, benchmarks, and evaluation results to the AI-on-demand platform, and validate demonstrator results through Testing and Experiment Facilities. Measurable target: open-source release achieving \u2265500 GitHub stars within six months of release; contributions accepted to the AI-on-demand platform; results validated through \u22652 Testing and Experiment Facilities (TEFs); technology transfer initiated through \u22653 European Digital Innovation Hubs (EDIHs).\n\nOBJ-8 \u2014 External Tool and API Orchestration Layer (ATU lead, Month 36): Develop and validate a cross-cutting orchestration layer providing a typed tool registry, formal tool selection and invocation policies integrated with the neuro-symbolic planning engine, standardised API adapters (REST, GraphQL, HL7 FHIR, OPC-UA), post-invocation verification and grounding, execution monitoring with fallback/recovery, and auditable tool execution traces \u2014 integrated architecturally across all three research pillars. Measurable target: typed tool registry supporting \u226530 external tools and APIs across all three demonstrator domains; tool invocation success rate \u226595%; mean recovery time from tool failure \u22645 seconds; 100% provenance trace coverage for all tool invocations.\n\nAll objectives are pertinent to the work programme topic, measurable against stated baselines and evaluation benchmarks, and realistically achievable within the 48-month timeframe given the consortium's established capabilities and access to operational deployment environments.\n\nBEYOND THE STATE OF THE ART\n\nCurrent AI agent research is distributed across three largely disconnected scientific communities. LLM-based agent frameworks \u2014 exemplified by ReAct and AutoGPT-style systems \u2014 excel at natural language task understanding but produce plans that degrade unpredictably over long task horizons, due to the absence of formal plan monitoring and the reliance on probabilistic chain-of-thought reasoning without verification. Classical planning and multi-agent systems provide formal correctness guarantees but cannot handle the ambiguity and open-endedness of real-world natural language instructions. Memory-augmented neural systems advance retrieval augmentation for improved single-turn accuracy but lack systematic integration with structured planning and multi-agent coordination. No existing system co-designs all four capability areas \u2014 structured planning and reasoning, adaptive memory management, decentralised multi-agent coordination, and principled external tool and API orchestration \u2014 into a single unified architecture.\n\nMAESTRO's exceptional contribution is precisely this co-design: the neuro-symbolic planning engine uses the adaptive memory architecture to maintain plan coherence over long horizons; the multi-agent coordination layer uses both planning and memory to coordinate heterogeneous agents with different capabilities and world models; and the External Tool and API Orchestration Layer is architecturally integrated across all three pillars \u2014 enabling agents to discover, select, invoke, verify, and compose external tools and APIs as first-class elements of their reasoning and action loops. The formal guarantees introduced by MAESTRO \u2014 verifiable sub-task decomposition with defined pre-conditions and post-conditions, protocol convergence proofs for multi-agent coordination, and post-invocation verification of tool outputs against domain constraints \u2014 represent a ground-breaking advance over existing probabilistic approaches that lack formal accountability. This integration is not achievable by combining off-the-shelf components from the three disconnected research communities, as the components share neither data representations nor evaluation interfaces. The project's scope was defined with reference to the published literature in LLM-based agents, classical planning (HTN, MCTS), multi-agent systems, and retrieval-augmented generation, confirming clear differentiation from existing work.\n\nR&I MATURITY\n\nThe three research pillars (WP2, WP3, WP4) commence at Technology Readiness Level 2, developing the theoretical and algorithmic foundations of a new class of AI agent architecture. By project end, all core capabilities target TRL 5: validated in relevant and operational environments through the healthcare demonstrator (WP5, NIHS \u2014 clinical validation against real diagnostic pathways), the manufacturing demonstrator (WP6, ISIA \u2014 validation in an operational pilot factory), and the logistics transfer demonstrator (WP7, ELI \u2014 validation across real international supply chain corridors). All demonstrators are co-designed with sector-leading industry partners who provide real deployment environments and domain-specific tool and API ecosystems. This TRL 2 to TRL 5 trajectory is consistent with the call's target readiness level (CC-01) and with the expectations for Research and Innovation Actions.",
      "word_count": 1083
```
