    {
      "sub_section_id": "B.1.2",
      "title": "Methodology",
      "content": "MAESTRO adopts a co-design methodology in which three research pillars and a cross-cutting orchestration capability are developed in parallel through tightly integrated work packages, governed by a shared data model, a unified cross-cutting evaluation framework (WP8, FIIT lead), and six-monthly integration checkpoints at which all pillar outputs are validated for interface compatibility and cross-demonstrator performance.\n\nOVERALL METHODOLOGY \u2014 CONCEPTS, MODELS, AND UNDERLYING ASSUMPTIONS\n\nPillar 1 \u2014 Neuro-Symbolic Planning and Reasoning (WP2, ATU lead; contributing partners CERIA, BIIS, BAL):\nTasks T2-01 through T2-03 develop, in sequence: sub-task graph decomposition with formally specified pre-conditions, post-conditions, and verification checkpoints; integration of MCTS and HTN planning algorithms with LLM-driven heuristic evaluation; and plan monitoring with self-correction that detects execution failures and replans from verified intermediate states rather than restarting from scratch. The central underlying assumption is that symbolic planning guarantees can be retained while LLM-driven heuristics dramatically reduce the search space branching factor, making formal planning tractable in open-ended natural language domains. The key challenge \u2014 managing computational overhead in high-branching-factor domains \u2014 is addressed through LLM-driven heuristic pruning that preserves formal verification at critical decision points while achieving tractable search. Deliverables: D2-01 (neuro-symbolic planning architecture specification, Month 18) and D2-02 (planning engine software prototype, Month 36).\n\nPillar 2 \u2014 Adaptive Memory Architecture (WP3, BIIS lead; contributing partners ATU, CERIA, BAL):\nTasks T3-01 through T3-03 develop a tri-store unified memory system: working memory (a structured, attention-managed short-term store maintaining the agent's current goals, active plan state, and recent observations), episodic memory (a retrieval-augmented store of past task episodes indexed by context similarity, enabling experience-based agent behaviour without retraining), and semantic memory (a persistent knowledge graph connecting domain concepts, tool capabilities, and learned task patterns). A learned memory controller governs information flow between all three stores, determining what to commit to long-term storage, what to retrieve, and when to forget \u2014 balancing recall accuracy against computational cost. The underlying model assumes that the three-store architecture mirrors established cognitive memory models and that retrieval-augmented approaches can efficiently index agent experience at scale. Deliverables: D3-01 (memory architecture design specification, Month 12) and D3-02 (adaptive memory system software, Month 30).\n\nPillar 3 \u2014 Decentralised Multi-Agent Coordination (WP4, CERIA lead; contributing partners ATU, BIIS):\nTasks T4-01 through T4-03 develop: a formal task-delegation protocol in which agents decompose tasks, negotiate subtask assignments, and establish shared commitment structures with provable convergence under partial observability; conflict resolution mechanisms for situations where agent plans interfere, resources are contested, or partial observations lead to inconsistent world models; and an auditable multi-agent interaction trace module producing structured traces that human operators can inspect and understand. The underlying model draws on game-theoretic mechanism design and formal verification of multi-agent protocols, extended to handle heterogeneous LLM-based agents with varying capabilities, world models, and tool access permissions. The key challenge is ensuring convergence under partial observability with heterogeneous agent types; CERIA's prior ERC Advanced Grant on formal methods for multi-agent systems provides the foundational methodology for addressing this. Deliverables: D4-01 (multi-agent coordination protocol specification, Month 18) and D4-02 (decentralised coordination software, Month 36).\n\nExternal Tool and API Orchestration Layer (ATU lead, architecturally integrated across WP2, WP3, and WP4):\nThe orchestration layer spans all three research pillars through six integrated components: a typed tool registry and capability model (with input/output schemas, preconditions, postconditions, cost profiles, and reliability metadata) that agents can query and reason over; formal tool selection and invocation policies integrated with the neuro-symbolic planning engine (Pillar 1), determining when and why to invoke an external tool versus relying on the agent's own reasoning based on task requirements, expected accuracy gains, and cost-latency trade-offs; standardised API adapters abstracting heterogeneous external protocols (REST, GraphQL, HL7 FHIR in healthcare, OPC-UA in manufacturing) into a uniform invocation interface; post-invocation validation mechanisms verifying tool outputs against expected schemas and domain constraints before incorporating results into agent state; runtime execution monitoring with timeout detection, error classification, and automated fallback strategies (alternative tool selection, graceful degradation, human-in-the-loop escalation) integrated with the planning engine's self-correction capability; and full provenance tracking for every tool invocation \u2014 recording requesting agent, planning rationale, invocation parameters, raw response, validation outcome, and downstream effect \u2014 stored in the adaptive memory architecture (Pillar 2) and accessible to the multi-agent coordination layer (Pillar 3) for delegation accountability. The key methodological challenge is protocol heterogeneity across the three demonstrator domains; the adapter framework addresses this through protocol-specific adapter modules presenting a uniform interface to all reasoning and planning layers.\n\nCross-Demonstrator Integration and Evaluation (WP8, FIIT lead; contributing partners ATU, CERIA, BIIS, ISIA, NIHS, ELI, BAL):\nTask T8-01 defines the cross-cutting evaluation framework and KPI definitions enabling consistent measurement across all three demonstrators. Task T8-02 integrates outputs from WP2, WP3, and WP4 into the unified MAESTRO framework. Task T8-03 conducts cross-demonstrator benchmarking and releases the MAESTRO benchmark suite (D8-02, Month 42) to the research community. The final integration and evaluation report (D8-03, Month 48) documents the architecture's cross-domain generalisability and provides the evidence base for future exploitation.\n\nNATIONAL AND INTERNATIONAL R&I ACTIVITIES FEEDING INTO THE PROJECT\n\nThe MAESTRO methodology builds explicitly on prior national and international R&I conducted by consortium partners. ATU has contributed to the AI-on-demand platform through a prior Horizon Europe project and served as WP lead for hybrid AI integration in a prior H2020 trustworthy AI project, providing the neuro-symbolic methodology and AI-on-demand integration experience for WP2 and OBJ-8 respectively. CERIA holds an ERC Advanced Grant on formal methods for multi-agent systems and has conducted coordination protocol design for autonomous multi-agent exploration under H2020, providing the formal verification and coordination protocol foundations for WP4. BIIS has conducted Horizon Europe research on unified transformers for text and retrieval and has participated in H2020 knowledge infrastructure projects, providing the neural memory and retrieval-augmented generation methodology for WP3. NIHS has participated in a Horizon Europe European Health Data Space pilot implementation project, establishing the clinical data infrastructure and validation pathways for WP5. ISIA has led Horizon Europe projects on AI for manufacturing process optimisation, providing the industrial deployment environment and smart manufacturing expertise for WP6. BAL leads Horizon Europe work on European large language models and holds EuroHPC access for large-scale LLM training, providing the LLM engineering foundations. FIIT has contributed to the AI-on-demand platform under H2020 and operates regional EDIHs, providing the benchmarking methodology and ecosystem linkage for WP8 and OBJ-7. The consortium will establish formal internal knowledge transfer protocols within WP1 to ensure relevant public results from prior EU-funded actions are systematically identified and built upon throughout the project.\n\nINTERDISCIPLINARY APPROACH\n\nMAESTRO is inherently and substantially interdisciplinary, integrating methods, data, and deployment environments from multiple scientific and engineering disciplines. Pillar 1 (WP2) integrates automated planning (classical AI), large language model research (machine learning), and formal verification (theoretical computer science). Pillar 2 (WP3) integrates information retrieval, knowledge representation and reasoning, and cognitive memory modelling. Pillar 3 (WP4) integrates game theory, distributed systems, and formal methods for multi-agent systems. The External Tool and API Orchestration Layer integrates software engineering (API adapter design, protocol abstraction), formal methods (tool selection policy specification), and AI system engineering (execution monitoring and fallback). The three demonstrator work packages integrate these computational foundations with: clinical medicine and health informatics (NIHS, WP5 \u2014 clinical decision support methodology, HL7 FHIR health data interoperability standards, and established clinical validation and ethics protocols); mechanical engineering, industrial IoT, digital twin modelling, and smart manufacturing systems engineering (ISIA, WP6 \u2014 OPC-UA industrial protocols, operational pilot factory environments, and process KPI frameworks); and logistics and supply chain management, multi-modal transport planning, and real-world operational data management (ELI, WP7 \u2014 international logistics corridor data and disruption recovery benchmarks). The evaluation and benchmarking methodology (WP8, FIIT) integrates AI benchmarking science, technology readiness assessment frameworks, and responsible AI evaluation practice. This breadth is reflected in the consortium composition spanning university AI research (ATU, BIIS, CERIA), domain-specific university expertise in medicine and engineering (NIHS, ISIA), industrial R&D in logistics and LLM engineering (ELI, BAL), and applied research and technology transfer (FIIT). Interdisciplinary integration is operationalised through: a shared data representation model across all three research pillars; co-designed benchmark scenarios jointly developed with industry partners from each sector; and six-monthly joint milestone reviews (WP8) attended by representatives of all disciplinary workstreams, ensuring that interdisciplinary interface issues are detected and resolved early.\n\nGENDER DIMENSION IN RESEARCH AND INNOVATION CONTENT\n\nThe gender dimension is relevant to MAESTRO's research content and is addressed primarily through the performance evaluation methodology of the demonstrators. In the healthcare demonstrator (WP5, NIHS), AI-assisted diagnostic reasoning is validated on de-identified clinical cases spanning five diagnostic domains; standard clinical AI benchmarking methodology requires evaluation of system performance across patient demographic subgroups including sex and gender, to identify performance disparities and ensure that AI-assisted clinical recommendations do not produce inequitable clinical outcomes. NIHS's ethics-approved de-identified clinical data repository (3M+ patient records) provides the data infrastructure to support this evaluation. In the manufacturing demonstrator (WP6, ISIA) and logistics demonstrator (WP7, ELI), gender dimensions arise in the context of human-AI interaction in industrial and operational settings, including user interface design and consideration of workforce diversity in operational environments deploying AI planning tools. The specific gender dimension analysis methodology for each demonstrator will be elaborated within the project management and quality plan (D1-01, Month 3, ATU) and within the respective use case specification deliverables (D5-01, D6-01, D7-01, all Month 18). The ethics compliance coordination task (T1-03, ATU) maintains oversight across all work packages to ensure the gender dimension is consistently reflected in demonstrator design, benchmarking protocols, and results reporting.\n\nOPEN SCIENCE PRACTICES\n\nMAESTRO implements open science practices proportionate to the scale and nature of the research. All communicable research outputs \u2014 frameworks, models, benchmarks, the External Tool and API Orchestration Layer, and demonstrator results \u2014 will be published as open-source software (D9-02, open-source software release, Month 36, BAL lead) and contributed to the AI-on-demand platform as specified in OBJ-7. The full MAESTRO benchmark suite (D8-02, Month 42, FIIT lead) will be released as open data for community adoption. Scientific publications will be published open-access. The dissemination and exploitation plan (D9-01, Month 6, BAL lead) establishes the consortium-wide open science strategy, including publication planning, data sharing protocols, and software licensing framework. End-user co-design is embedded in the demonstrator validation methodology: clinical experts at NIHS co-design and validate healthcare diagnostic benchmarks (T5-01, T5-03); manufacturing engineers and process specialists at ISIA co-design production optimisation KPI frameworks (T6-01); logistics specialists at ELI co-design operational validation scenarios and disruption benchmarks (T7-01). Citizens and civil society are engaged through public communication activities coordinated by WP9 (BAL), including project website, public events, and science communication. Engagement with the AI-on-demand platform community constitutes the primary channel for sharing results with the European R&D community and for civil society and research community engagement at scale.\n\nDATA MANAGEMENT PLAN\n\nA comprehensive Data Management Plan (DMP) will be provided as a distinct deliverable within the first six months of the project (D1-02, Month 6, ATU lead), ensuring that all project research data is managed in accordance with FAIR principles (Findable, Accessible, Interoperable, Reusable). The DMP will cover: de-identified clinical benchmark datasets managed by NIHS under established ethics approvals and the NIHS clinical research ethics infrastructure; manufacturing operational process data managed by ISIA under confidentiality agreements with industry partners and in compliance with applicable data protection legislation; logistics operational data managed by ELI in anonymised form across 30+ countries of operation; open benchmark datasets for community release (MAESTRO benchmark suite, D8-02, FIIT); and open-source model and code artefacts released under open licences. Data management procedures will comply with Horizon Europe requirements and applicable data protection legislation, including GDPR where personal or clinically derived data are involved.",

      "title": "Project's pathways towards impact",
      "content": "MAESTRO makes a specific, traceable contribution to both the call expected outcomes and the wider expected impacts of the destination 'Achieving open strategic autonomy in digital and emerging enabling technologies (2026-27)'. Each pathway described below is grounded in concrete WP deliverables and consortium partner activities; quantified estimates are drawn from project impact KPIs defined in Phase 5.\n\n(a) Unique contribution towards call expected outcomes and wider impacts\n\nContribution to EO-01 \u2014 Significant improvements in AI agent autonomy, robustness and reliability: MAESTRO advances the three foundational architectural pillars constraining current AI agent autonomy at TRL 5 by M36. (i) The ATU-led neuro-symbolic planning engine (WP2; D2-01, D2-02) integrates MCTS and HTN symbolic planning with LLM heuristics and formal pre/post-condition verification, enabling verifiable sub-task graph decomposition and plan self-correction \u2014 directly eliminating the unverifiable single-step prompting that limits reliability in deployed systems. (ii) The BIIS-led adaptive tri-store memory architecture (WP3; D3-01, D3-02) unifies working, episodic and semantic memory with a learned controller, enabling long-horizon coherence across extended interactions without retraining. (iii) The CERIA-led external tool and API orchestration layer (WP2/WP8; D8-01) provides a typed tool registry, formal tool selection policies and post-invocation verification, removing brittleness from untyped tool calls. Together these outputs achieve statistically significant improvement over state-of-the-art baselines on \u22653 benchmark task dimensions (KPI-11, p<0.05, MAESTRO benchmark suite D8-02, WP8-FIIT).\n\nContribution to EO-02 \u2014 Innovative multi-agent frameworks for effective decentralised coordination: CERIA's formally verified multi-agent coordination protocol suite (WP4; D4-01, D4-02) provides task-delegation, negotiation and conflict-resolution protocols with mathematically proven convergence guarantees for heterogeneous agents under partial observability. The auditable multi-agent interaction trace module (T4-03) enables full auditability of inter-agent coordination. These protocols are operationally validated across three sector demonstrators (WP5, WP6, WP7), each requiring coordination of specialist sub-agents in live operational environments, providing multi-sector evidence of performance beyond the capabilities of individual agents.\n\nContribution to EI-01 \u2014 Implementation of the European Apply AI Strategy (healthcare, advanced manufacturing, in-vehicle autonomous driving): Three TRL-5 sector demonstrators constitute MAESTRO's direct implementation of the Apply AI Strategy's three prioritised sectors. NIHS deploys multi-specialist-agent clinical decision support on 500 de-identified clinical cases with HL7 FHIR integration (WP5; D5-01, D5-02), producing EU AI Act high-risk system compliance evidence and engaging \u22653 European hospital networks in formal post-project adoption planning by M48 (KPI-01). ISIA deploys manufacturing process optimisation agents with digital twin integration across production segments in an operational factory environment (WP6; D6-01, D6-02), targeting \u226515% defect reduction and \u226510% energy savings against defined KPIs (KPI-02). ELI validates MAESTRO generalisation across \u22653 international supply chain corridors (WP7; D7-01, D7-02), targeting \u226520% improvement in disruption recovery time (KPI-03), and produces a formal architectural transferability mapping to in-vehicle autonomous driving, confirming MAESTRO's reach across all three Apply AI Strategy sectors. The specific contribution of this project \u2014 not of AI R&I in general \u2014 is that the same validated MAESTRO planning, memory, coordination, and tool orchestration architecture underpins all three demonstrators, providing sector-specific evidence for a unified European AI agent framework.\n\nContribution to EI-02 \u2014 Wider industrial deployment and uptake via EDIHs: MAESTRO's EDIH-mediated deployment operates through three coordinated channels grounded in WP9. All three channels are coordinated through signed EDIH partnership agreements monitored under WP9.\n\nContribution to EI-03 \u2014 Open scientific advancement and sharing of AI agent R&D results via AI-on-demand: ATU, BIIS, CERIA and FIIT target \u226520 peer-reviewed publications in NeurIPS, ICML, ICLR, AAMAS and AAAI (KPI-06), with \u22653 invited keynotes, from M12 to M60. All publications are deposited in open-access repositories under Plan S-compliant CC-BY licence within six months of acceptance. FIIT releases the MAESTRO benchmark suite dataset (D8-02, M36) as community evaluation infrastructure on the AI-on-demand platform, targeting adoption by \u22655 external research groups by M48 (KPI-07) and \u2265100 portfolio citations within three years (KPI-09). The open-source MAESTRO framework (D9-02, BAL, M36) provides shared European AI agent research infrastructure accessible to the European research community without proprietary access barriers.\n\nContribution to EI-04 \u2014 Open strategic autonomy in digital and emerging enabling technologies [Note: This impact is inferred from the topic's destination placement in the work programme; no explicit expected-impact statement for strategic autonomy was confirmed in the call scope or expected outcome sections \u2014 see PATH-EI-04 in impact_architecture.json]: MAESTRO's European-origin foundational capabilities \u2014 neuro-symbolic planning engine (D2-02, WP2-ATU), formally verified coordination protocols (D4-01, D4-02, WP4-CERIA), and open-source framework (D9-02, WP9-BAL) \u2014 provide sovereign AI agent infrastructure differentiated by auditability and formal verifiability rather than parameter scale alone. CERIA's D4-01 protocol specification forms the basis for \u22651 formal standardisation submission to ISO/IEC JTC 1/SC 42 or IEEE Standards Association by M48 (KPI-08), accompanied by an EU AI Act multi-agent transparency alignment report, directly extending EU strategic autonomy from research output into international AI governance norm-setting.\n\nContribution to EI-05 \u2014 Unlocking the economic potential of AI agents across diverse sectors including data analytics and coding: The neuro-symbolic planning engine (D2-02) enables verifiable multi-step goal decomposition for analytical, coding and financial workflows where execution failures are costly. The external tool and API orchestration layer (D8-01, OUT-9, WP2/WP8) provides typed API integration and post-invocation verification as a prerequisite for economically deployable agentic workflows in any sector. The adaptive memory system (D3-02) unlocks long-horizon agent applications in legal research, financial analysis and software development. Mitigating measure: EDIH and EIT Manufacturing intermediary partnerships (BAL, WP9) provide structured adoption facilitation; the open-source community ecosystem creates adoption dynamics that persist post-project through operational dependency.\n\nIn-vehicle autonomous driving sector transfer: Full validation in the automotive domain is beyond the scope and duration of this project. WP7 (D7-02, ELI) produces formal architectural transferability mapping to in-vehicle autonomous driving as a foundation for post-project follow-on, rather than claiming full sector deployment within the project timeline.\n\nClinical data access: Ethics approval timelines and data governance requirements constrain clinical data availability for WP5 validation. The \u226515% defect reduction and \u226510% energy savings demonstrated in the WP6 pilot factory (KPI-02) constitute the commercially transferable value proposition for SME adoption.\n\nLogistics operational integration (ELI; M42\u2013M48): A confirmed integration roadmap for MAESTRO multi-agent coordination capabilities into ELI's operational supply chain management systems, targeting commercial deployment across \u22653 international logistics corridors and establishing ELI as an anchor European commercial operator for AI agent-driven supply chain resilience.\n\nOpen-source ecosystem (BAL; M36\u2013M60): \u226510 European SMEs and startups actively building production AI agent applications on the MAESTRO open-source framework by M48 (D9-02, KPI-04), creating a self-sustaining European AI agent application ecosystem that reduces platform dependency on non-European proprietary solutions and generates downstream commercial AI agent products.\n\nStandardisation and protocol adoption (CERIA; M42\u2013M54): MAESTRO formally verified coordination protocol specification (D4-01) submitted to \u22651 standardisation body (KPI-08) and adopted as reference architecture by \u22653 external multi-agent AI research projects, with normative embedding extending MAESTRO's commercial and regulatory reach through international standards.\n\nIntellectual property strategy: MAESTRO applies an open-core IPR approach calibrated to maximise European ecosystem adoption while preserving commercial exploitation pathways for sector-specific partners. The core framework, benchmark suite, evaluation infrastructure and coordination protocol specifications are released under Apache 2.0, jointly owned by the consortium, to lower barriers for European SMEs and startups and to support the AI-on-demand platform contribution mandate. Sector-specific demonstrator configurations, GDPR-anonymised clinical validation datasets, and industrial deployment parameters may be protected as trade secrets or licensed commercially by NIHS (clinical), ISIA (manufacturing) and ELI (logistics). CERIA retains attribution rights for standardisation submissions with consortium consent. BAL leads IPR management coordination under WP9 T9-02 and maintains the consortium IP register, ensuring that open-source release decisions do not unintentionally foreclose commercial licensing paths for any partner.\n\nCommunication\n\nBAL leads all public communication activities through WP9 T9-03: a project website live by M3; active social media channels targeting AI practitioners, industry decision-makers and policy audiences; and open public webinars on European AI agent development at M24 and M48. Main messages are calibrated to each target group: scientific novelty of the MAESTRO architecture for the research community; sector-specific performance gains and regulatory compliance pathways for industrial stakeholders; and European AI sovereignty and ecosystem contributions for policy audiences. The data management plan (D1-02, ATU, M6) governs FAIR (Findable, Accessible, Interoperable, Reusable) compliance and open access timelines for all project outputs. Sensitive clinical validation data from WP5 is anonymised per GDPR and EU AI Act requirements before any public release; the de-identified evaluation dataset (D5-02) is published as open data on the AI-on-demand platform.\n\nPolicy feedback: MAESTRO generates direct policy feedback for EU AI Act multi-agent system transparency requirements through CERIA's EU AI Act multi-agent transparency alignment report (M48). WP5 clinical demonstrator results (NIHS) inform the intersection of EU medical device regulation with EU AI Act high-risk AI diagnostic system requirements. These policy feedback contributions are documented in D9-03 (final dissemination and impact report, BAL, M48).\n\nSustainability: Post-project sustainability is grounded in three reinforcing mechanisms documented in the Phase 5 impact architecture. First, the open-source MAESTRO framework creates self-sustaining community maintenance dynamics once \u226510 European SMEs and startups build production applications on it by M48. Second, operational embedding at NIHS, ISIA and ELI generates post-project maintenance through live commercial operational requirements, ensuring technology is sustained through existing revenue streams rather than requiring grant continuation. Third, CERIA's standardisation submissions embed MAESTRO coordination protocols as normative international reference architecture, ensuring the coordination design persists in the standards landscape independently of any single organisation. BAL coordinates long-term exploitation strategy through WP9 and produces the final dissemination and impact report (D9-03, M48) documenting community governance handover.",

      "content": "OVERALL WORK PLAN STRUCTURE\n\nMAESTRO organises its 48-month research programme into nine work packages (WP1\u2013WP9) structured across four functional layers proportionate to the scale and complexity of an 8-partner RIA addressing three research pillars and three demonstrator domains. The management layer (WP1, lead ATU) provides consortium governance, quality assurance, and ethics compliance \u2014 including mandatory cohesion activities with ADRA and the GenAI4EU central Hub (SR-09; CC-03/CC-04) \u2014 throughout the project. The research pillar layer (WP2\u2013WP4) develops the three foundational MAESTRO capabilities in parallel: neuro-symbolic planning and reasoning (WP2, lead ATU), adaptive memory architecture (WP3, lead BIIS), and decentralised multi-agent coordination (WP4, lead CERIA). The application and validation layer (WP5\u2013WP7) validates the integrated MAESTRO framework in three real-world application domains: healthcare clinical decision support (WP5, lead NIHS), manufacturing process optimisation (WP6, lead ISIA), and logistics supply chain operations (WP7, lead ELI), satisfying the Apply AI sector requirement of SR-07. The horizontal layer (WP8\u2013WP9) integrates the research pillars, manages cross-demonstrator evaluation and benchmarking aligned with SR-06/CC-06 (WP8, lead FIIT), and executes dissemination, exploitation, and AI-on-demand platform contributions required under SR-10 and CC-05 (WP9, lead BAL).\n\nTABLE 3.1a \u2014 LIST OF WORK PACKAGES\n\nWP1: Project Management and Coordination | Lead: ATU | M1\u2013M48\nWP2: Neuro-Symbolic Planning and Reasoning Engine | Lead: ATU | M1\u2013M36\nWP3: Adaptive Memory Architecture | Lead: BIIS | M1\u2013M30\nWP4: Decentralised Multi-Agent Coordination | Lead: CERIA | M3\u2013M36\nWP5: Healthcare Demonstrator \u2014 Clinical Decision Support | Lead: NIHS | M12\u2013M42\nWP6: Manufacturing Demonstrator \u2014 Process Optimisation | Lead: ISIA | M12\u2013M42\nWP7: Logistics Transfer Demonstrator \u2014 Cross-Sector Generalisation | Lead: ELI | M12\u2013M42\nWP8: Integration, Evaluation and Benchmarking | Lead: FIIT | M6\u2013M48\nWP9: Dissemination, Exploitation and Communication | Lead: BAL | M1\u2013M48\n\nPerson-month allocations per WP and partner are confirmed as structurally consistent in the validated budget response (budget gate assessment: pass; validation ref: budget_validation_response_2026-04-24T14:30:00Z.json). Specific figures are drawn exclusively from that validated response.\n\nTABLE 3.1b \u2014 WORK PACKAGE DESCRIPTIONS\n\nWP1 (Lead: ATU; contributing: CERIA, BIIS, ISIA, NIHS, ELI, BAL, FIIT; M1\u2013M48). Objectives: (1) Ensure effective consortium governance, administrative management, and reporting. (2) Maintain quality assurance, risk management, and ethics compliance across all project activities. Tasks: T1-01 Consortium governance and financial management (M1\u2013M48, ATU) \u2014 covers financial management, grant agreement compliance, EC/ADRA liaison, and GenAI4EU Hub cohesion per CC-03/CC-04; T1-02 Quality assurance and risk monitoring (M1\u2013M48, ATU) \u2014 manages the risk register and milestone reviews; T1-03 Ethics compliance oversight and coordination with GenAI4EU Hub (M1\u2013M48, ATU) \u2014 oversees ethics self-assessment categories 2, 4, and 8 and satisfies mandatory cohesion requirement of SR-09.\n\nWP2 (Lead: ATU; contributing: CERIA, BIIS, BAL; M1\u2013M36). Objectives: (1) Design and implement a hybrid neuro-symbolic planning engine with formal sub-task graph decomposition. (2) Integrate MCTS and HTN planning with LLM-based heuristics and verifiable plan self-correction. Addresses SR-02 (robust planning and reasoning) and SR-01 (next-generation AI agents). Tasks: T2-01 Sub-task graph decomposition design with formal pre/post-conditions (M1\u2013M12, ATU) \u2014 establishes the formal planning substrate; T2-02 MCTS and HTN planning integration with LLM heuristics (M6\u2013M24, ATU) \u2014 integrates neural and symbolic planning methods; T2-03 Plan monitoring and self-correction implementation (M18\u2013M36, ATU) \u2014 completes the engine with verifiable self-correction. WP2 outputs feed directly into WP5, WP6, WP7 (planning capability for demonstrators) and WP8 (unified framework integration).\n\nWP3 (Lead: BIIS; contributing: ATU, CERIA, BAL; M1\u2013M30). Objectives: (1) Design and implement a unified tri-store memory architecture with a learned memory controller. (2) Develop memory indexing, retrieval, and forgetting mechanisms for long-horizon agent interactions. Addresses SR-03 (effective memory and state management). Tasks: T3-01 Tri-store memory architecture design (M1\u2013M12, BIIS) \u2014 establishes working, episodic, and semantic memory stores; T3-02 Memory indexing and retrieval strategy implementation (M6\u2013M24, BIIS) \u2014 enables efficient retrieval across long-horizon interactions; T3-03 Forgetting mechanism and coherence maintenance (M18\u2013M30, BIIS) \u2014 ensures temporal coherence. WP3 outputs feed into WP5, WP6, WP7, and WP8.\n\nWP4 (Lead: CERIA; contributing: ATU, BIIS; M3\u2013M36). Objectives: (1) Develop formally specified task-delegation and negotiation protocols for heterogeneous AI agents. (2) Demonstrate convergence guarantees and auditable multi-agent interaction with shared tool access governance. Tasks: T4-01 Task-delegation and negotiation protocol design (M3\u2013M15, CERIA) \u2014 produces the formal protocol specification with convergence properties; T4-02 Convergence and conflict resolution under partial observability (M12\u2013M24, CERIA) \u2014 addresses real-world coordination challenges; T4-03 Auditable multi-agent interaction trace module (M18\u2013M36, CERIA) \u2014 enables verifiable multi-agent behaviour logging. WP4 outputs feed into WP5, WP6, WP7, and WP8.\n\nWP5 (Lead: NIHS; contributing: ATU, BIIS, BAL, FIIT; M12\u2013M42). (2) Produce a standardised benchmark suite for community adoption and cross-demonstrator evaluation. Addresses SR-06/CC-06 (KPIs, benchmarking, progress monitoring) and SR-11/CC-07 (AI Factories and Testing and Experiment Facilities linkage). Depends on WP5, WP6, WP7. Tasks: T8-01 Cross-cutting evaluation framework and KPI definition (M6\u2013M12, FIIT) \u2014 establishes shared evaluation metrics early so all pillar WPs are measured consistently; T8-02 MAESTRO unified framework integration (M18\u2013M42, FIIT) \u2014 integrates WP2, WP3, WP4 outputs into a deployable unified framework; T8-03 Cross-demonstrator benchmarking and community benchmark release (M42\u2013M48, FIIT). (2) Develop and execute consortium exploitation strategy and lead public communication. Depends on WP8. Tasks: T9-03 Communication, website, and public engagement (M1\u2013M48, BAL) \u2014 runs continuously; T9-02 Exploitation strategy development and IP management (M3\u2013M36, BAL); T9-01 Open-source release management and community building (M18\u2013M48, BAL) \u2014 manages the open-source release and AI-on-demand platform contributions.\n\nTABLE 3.1c \u2014 LIST OF DELIVERABLES\n\nD1-01 Project management and quality plan (WP1, ATU, R, PU, M3); D7-01 Logistics demonstrator specification and benchmark report (WP7, ELI, R, PU, M24); D7-02 Cross-sector generalisation evaluation dataset (WP7, ELI, DATA, PU, M42); D8-01 Evaluation framework and benchmark specification (WP8, FIIT, R, PU, M12); D8-02 MAESTRO benchmark suite dataset (WP8, FIIT, DATA, PU, M42); D8-03 Final integration and evaluation report (WP8, FIIT, R, PU, M48); D9-01 Dissemination and exploitation plan (WP9, BAL, R, PU, M6) \u2014 admissibility condition, mandatory distinct deliverable within 6 months; D9-02 Open-source software release (WP9, BAL, OTHER, PU, M36); D9-03 Final dissemination and impact report (WP9, BAL, R, PU, M48). Type codes: R=document/report; OTHER=software; DATA=data set. Dissemination levels: PU=public fully open; SEN=sensitive (applied to clinical data deliverables in WP5 reflecting GDPR obligations for special-category health data).\n\nTIMELINE AND GANTT CHART NARRATIVE\n\nThe 48-month timeline unfolds in four overlapping phases. Phase 1 (M1\u2013M12) establishes integration contracts and architecture specifications (MS1, M3), early research foundations across all three pillars, and demonstrator use case definitions (MS5, M12). Phase 2 (M12\u2013M24) completes pillar prototype development (MS2 planning engine v1.0, M12; MS3 memory architecture v1.0, M12; MS4 multi-agent protocol with convergence proofs, M15) and achieves Integrated MAESTRO Framework v1.0 with all three pillars and the tool orchestration layer operating together (MS6, M24). Phase 3 (M24\u2013M42) deploys the framework in all three demonstrator environments (MS7, M30), confirms research pillar quantitative targets (MS8, M36), and completes full cross-demonstrator validation (MS9, M42). Phase 4 (M42\u2013M48) delivers the community benchmark suite, open-source release and AI-on-demand platform publication (MS10, M45), and final project closure (MS11, M48). Management (WP1 T1-01/T1-02/T1-03) and communication (WP9 T9-03) tasks run continuously throughout M1\u2013M48.\n\nThe critical path runs through the neuro-symbolic planning pillar (T2-01 M1\u2013M12, T2-02 M6\u2013M24, T2-03 M18\u2013M36), through the healthcare demonstrator (T5-01 M12\u2013M18, T5-02 M18\u2013M36, T5-03 M36\u2013M42), and concludes with cross-demonstrator benchmarking (T8-03 M42\u2013M48). Nine structurally equivalent critical paths of equal length (three dependency edges) have been identified, reflecting the symmetric dependency structure: each of WP2, WP3, and WP4 feeds each of WP5, WP6, and WP7, which all feed WP8, which feeds WP9. Delay in any research pillar will therefore cascade to at least one demonstrator and to the integration timeline. The dependency graph is confirmed as a directed acyclic graph with no cycles (Kahn algorithm verified, 36 nodes processed).\n\nTABLE 3.1d \u2014 LIST OF MILESTONES\n\nMS1 (M3, WP1, ATU): Architecture specification and integration contracts finalised. Verification: shared data representations, API contracts, and integration interfaces for all three pillars reviewed and accepted by all pillar leads; tool registry schema and integration test harness operational.\nMS2 (M12, WP2, ATU): Planning engine v1.0 \u2014 baseline neuro-symbolic integration. Verification: decomposition of \u22655 benchmark task types with verifiable pre/post-conditions; measurable improvement over LLM-only baseline on \u22651 standardised agent benchmark.\nMS3 (M12, WP3, BIIS): Memory architecture v1.0 \u2014 tri-store prototype operational. Verification: all three memory stores individually operational; coherence improvement over context-window-only baseline on synthetic long-horizon tasks (>20 steps).\nMS4 (M15, WP4, CERIA): Multi-agent protocol specification with convergence proofs. Verification: formal protocol specification complete; convergence proofs for \u22653 core task classes; simulation validation with \u22655 heterogeneous agents.\nMS5 (M12, WP8, FIIT): Demonstrator use cases defined and domain data secured. Verification: clinical use cases, manufacturing scenarios, and logistics corridors fully specified with acceptance criteria; ethics approvals for clinical data granted; factory access agreement signed; logistics data access terms agreed.\nMS6 (M24, WP8, FIIT): Integrated MAESTRO framework v1.0 with tool orchestration layer. Verification: all three pillars and tool orchestration layer integrated; tool registry populated with \u226510 tools/APIs; end-to-end evaluation on cross-cutting benchmarks; framework deployable in all demonstrator environments.\nMS7 (M30, WP8, FIIT): Demonstrator v1.0 \u2014 initial deployment in all three demonstrator environments. Verification: MAESTRO deployed in healthcare, manufacturing, and logistics environments; domain-specific adapters operational; initial functional evaluation completed in each sector.\nMS8 (M36, WP2, ATU): Research pillar targets achieved. Verification: \u226540% plan success improvement (OBJ-1); \u226530% memory coherence improvement (OBJ-2); \u226525% joint task completion improvement (OBJ-3); all results reproducible and documented.\nMS9 (M42, WP8, FIIT): Demonstrator validation complete \u2014 all environments. Verification: healthcare validated on 500 clinical cases (OBJ-4); manufacturing validated over 3-month operational period (OBJ-5); logistics validated across 3 corridors (OBJ-6); tool orchestration validated with \u226530 tools/APIs registered (OBJ-8); cross-demonstrator evaluation report completed; architectural transferability to in-vehicle autonomous driving mapped.\nMS10 (M45, WP9, BAL): Open-source release and platform contributions delivered. Verification: MAESTRO framework released as open-source on GitHub; benchmark suite published on AI-on-demand platform (SR-10, CC-05); documentation and tutorials available; EDIH dissemination initiated in \u22653 hubs.\nMS11 (M48, WP1, ATU): Project completion and final review. Verification: all deliverables submitted; final exploitation plans per partner delivered; TEF validation reports completed; final review documentation compiled.\n\nTABLE 3.1e \u2014 CRITICAL RISKS FOR IMPLEMENTATION\n\nEvaluators assess risk management as part of the Quality and efficiency criterion. The MAESTRO risk register identifies eleven implementation risks across technical, regulatory, operational, and management categories. The highest-severity risks and their mitigations are:\n\nRISK-01 (WP2, technical, medium likelihood, high impact): Neuro-symbolic integration performance. Mitigation: modular architecture with well-defined symbolic/neural interfaces; LLM-only planner fallback modes for latency-critical scenarios; integration testing commencing M6 rather than M18. Contingency: deliver symbolic planning as a post-hoc verification layer if full co-generation is not achievable at TRL 5.\n\nRISK-04 (WP5, regulatory, medium likelihood, high impact): Clinical dataset access delayed or restricted by ethics review. Mitigation: ethics applications submitted in M1 (pre-project preparation initiated); publicly available clinical datasets (MIMIC-IV, eICU) as interim validation sources; data abstraction layer enabling seamless data source switching. Contingency: exclusively public clinical benchmarks with synthetic patient data if proprietary access is blocked.\n\nRISK-07 (WP2/WP3/WP4/WP8, technical, high likelihood, medium impact): Rapid LLM advancement changing baseline assumptions. Mitigation: model-agnostic interfaces across all MAESTRO components; annual baseline re-evaluation at M12, M24, M36. MAESTRO's value lies in the architecture (planning, memory, coordination) not in any specific LLM.\n\nRISK-09 (WP1, management, low likelihood, high impact): Partner withdrawal or key personnel departure. Mitigation: each pillar covered by \u22652 partners with relevant expertise; deputy PI appointments for each WP lead; consortium agreement commitment clauses and transition procedures.\n\nRISK-10 (WP2/WP3/WP4/WP8, technical, medium likelihood, high impact): Framework integration complexity across independently developed pillars. Mitigation: shared data representations, API contracts, and tool registry schemas defined in M1\u2013M3 (MS1, WP8 early deliverable); integration checkpoints every 6 months; BAL assigned as cross-pillar integration engineer. Contingency: composition-based approach (lightweight orchestration layer) if deep integration proves infeasible.\n\nRISK-11 (WP2/WP3/WP5/WP6/WP7/WP8, technical, medium likelihood, medium impact): External tool and API heterogeneity across three demonstrator domains (HL7 FHIR, OPC-UA, logistics APIs). Mitigation: minimal common adapter interface defined in M1\u2013M3; prioritisation of most critical APIs per demonstrator; reuse of existing open-source connector libraries. Full risk register with all eleven risks (RISK-01 through RISK-11) is held in the implementation architecture artifact (risk_register_ref).\n\nTABLES 3.1f\u20133.1h \u2014 STAFF EFFORT, SUBCONTRACTING, AND EQUIPMENT\n\nPerson-month allocations per participant per work package (Table 3.1f), subcontracting cost items (Table 3.1g), and major equipment purchase costs (Table 3.1h) are governed exclusively by the validated Lump Sum Budget Planner response. The budget gate assessment confirms structural consistency: all nine work packages (WP1\u2013WP9) and all eight consortium partners (ATU, CERIA, BIIS, ISIA, NIHS, ELI, BAL, FIIT) are confirmed present in the validated budget with no blocking inconsistencies. The effort distribution is consistent with WP lead responsibilities as documented in the work package structure and partner roles. No specific budget figures are introduced in this narrative; all cost data is drawn exclusively from the validated budget response held in the integration received directory.",

      "title": "Capacity of participants and consortium as a whole",
      "content": "CONSORTIUM COMPOSITION AND MATCH TO PROJECT OBJECTIVES\n\nThe MAESTRO consortium comprises eight organisations across six EU and associated countries, combining the full range of expertise and infrastructure required to develop, validate, and transfer next-generation AI agent capabilities to real-world application sectors. The consortium matches MAESTRO's objectives precisely: three research universities and institutes lead the three foundational research pillars (ATU, CERIA, BIIS); three domain organisations lead validation in the three Apply AI sectors (NIHS, ISIA, ELI); one private AI lab provides LLM engineering and open-source platform capacity across all work packages (BAL); and one applied research and technology centre provides evaluation rigour, benchmarking, and EDIH technology transfer capacity (FIIT). Each partner has a clearly defined, non-overlapping primary role and has demonstrated the capabilities and infrastructure necessary to fulfil it.\n\nATU \u2014 Alpenstadt Technical University (DE, HES; coordinator; WP1 and WP2 lead): ATU's Chair of AI Foundations has pioneered work in neuro-symbolic AI, automated planning, and LLM-based reasoning systems \u2014 precisely the expertise required to lead the neuro-symbolic planning pillar (WP2, addressing SR-02). As project coordinator, ATU provides consortium governance, financial management, EC and ADRA liaison (CC-03), and GenAI4EU Hub cohesion coordination (CC-04). ATU also contributes to WP3 (memory integration), WP4 (protocol design), WP5 (clinical demonstrator support), WP8 (unified framework integration), and WP9 (dissemination).\n\nCERIA \u2014 Centre Europ\u00e9en de Recherche en Informatique Avanc\u00e9e (FR, REC; WP4 lead): CERIA's multi-agent systems team has extensive expertise in formal coordination protocols, distributed AI, and game-theoretic multi-agent cooperation. This makes CERIA uniquely suited to lead WP4, which delivers the formally specified task-delegation and negotiation protocols with convergence guarantees that all three demonstrators depend upon. CERIA also contributes formal verification expertise to WP2 and WP3, and supports the logistics demonstrator coordination scenarios in WP7 and framework integration in WP8.\n\nBIIS \u2014 Breda Institute for Intelligent Systems (NL, HES; WP3 lead): BIIS is a pioneer in retrieval-augmented generation and memory-augmented neural networks, hosting leading research groups in deep learning and information retrieval. This expertise directly corresponds to the tri-store adaptive memory architecture objectives of WP3, which addresses SR-03. BIIS also contributes to WP2 (memory-planning integration), WP4 (memory-coordination interfaces), WP5 (clinical long-horizon interaction memory), and WP8.\n\nISIA \u2014 Istituto Superiore di Ingegneria Avanzata (IT, HES; WP6 lead): ISIA's AI for Manufacturing lab has extensive operational experience in digital twins, smart factory systems, and AI-driven process optimisation. This expertise is directly relevant to WP6, where ISIA provides the pilot factory environment and manufacturing domain knowledge for the advanced manufacturing demonstrator (SR-07). ISIA's digital twin infrastructure mitigates RISK-05 (factory access disruption) by enabling high-fidelity simulation during development phases. ISIA contributes to WP1, WP8, and WP9.\n\nNIHS \u2014 Nordic Institute of Health Sciences (SE, HES; WP5 lead): NIHS's Centre for Health Informatics conducts research on AI-assisted clinical decision support and clinical NLP, and provides access to de-identified clinical datasets and established clinical validation pathways. This healthcare-specific infrastructure and expertise is essential for WP5, the healthcare demonstrator (SR-07). NIHS also holds primary responsibility for ethics oversight of healthcare data handling, governing GDPR compliance for special-category health data (ETHICS-02) and Category 2 human participant considerations (ETHICS-03). NIHS contributes to WP1 and WP8.\n\nELI \u2014 EuroLog International AG (CH, PRC; WP7 lead): ELI is a major European logistics company operating in over 80 countries, with an Innovation Lab focused on AI-powered logistics optimisation and autonomous planning systems. ELI provides the unique combination of real-world logistics operations data and operational deployment environments across three international corridors required for the cross-sector transfer demonstrator (WP7). ELI's commercial role in MAESTRO ensures direct exploitation routes into logistics sector adoption and provides an industrial anchor for the framework's generalisation claim. ELI contributes to WP1, WP8, and WP9.\n\nBAL \u2014 Boreal AI Labs Oy (FI, PRC; WP9 lead): BAL is a leading European private AI lab specialising in building custom large language models, LLM fine-tuning, and production-grade AI deployment. BAL's expertise bridges the research and application layers of MAESTRO: BAL contributes LLM integration and deployment engineering to all six research and demonstrator WPs (WP2, WP3, WP4, WP5, WP6, WP7) and leads WP9, managing open-source release, AI-on-demand platform contributions (SR-10, CC-05), and consortium exploitation strategy. BAL's role as cross-pillar integration engineer (RISK-10 mitigation) is essential for the unified framework integration in WP8.\n\nFIIT \u2014 Fundaci\u00f3n Ib\u00e9rica de Innovaci\u00f3n Tecnol\u00f3gica (ES, REC; WP8 lead): FIIT's AI and Data Analytics division leads work on AI evaluation frameworks, benchmarking methodologies, and technology transfer through European Digital Innovation Hubs (EDIHs). FIIT is the evaluation and integration spine of MAESTRO, leading WP8 to define the cross-cutting evaluation framework and KPIs (SR-06, CC-06), integrate all research pillars into a unified deployable system, coordinate with AI Factories and Testing and Experiment Facilities (SR-11, CC-07), and drive EDIH network dissemination. FIIT contributes to WP5, WP6, WP7, and WP9.\n\nCOMPLEMENTARITY AND COVERAGE OF THE VALUE CHAIN\n\nThe consortium covers the full value chain from fundamental AI research through applied domain validation to industrial deployment and European community scaling. The three research pillar leads (ATU, CERIA, BIIS) together address all four research areas of SR-05: advanced self-planning and self-optimisation (WP2, ATU), memory-augmented agents for long-term reasoning (WP3, BIIS), advanced multi-agent frameworks for collaborative agents (WP4, CERIA), and external tool and API integration (SR-04) addressed across all pillar WPs. The three demonstrator leads (NIHS, ISIA, ELI) cover the three Apply AI sectors explicitly identified in SR-07 and CC-10: healthcare, advanced manufacturing, and logistics (providing cross-sector transfer evidence for the in-vehicle autonomous driving sector). BAL bridges the research and deployment layers; FIIT bridges the research and policy/industry transfer layers. No partner duplicates another's primary competence. Each partner is both necessary for and sufficient within its primary role.\n\nACCESS TO CRITICAL INFRASTRUCTURE\n\nNIHS provides de-identified clinical datasets and established clinical validation pathways for WP5 healthcare demonstrator development and validation. ISIA provides a pilot factory environment with digital twin infrastructure for WP6 manufacturing demonstrator deployment. ELI provides real-world logistics operational data and multi-corridor deployment environments for WP7 cross-sector transfer validation. ATU, CERIA, and BIIS bring research computing infrastructure for algorithmic development and training. FIIT connects MAESTRO to AI-on-demand platform infrastructure (CC-05, SR-10) and EDIH networks for technology transfer (CC-07, SR-11).\n\nGENDER EQUALITY PLANS\n\nPartners ATU (DE, HES), CERIA (FR, REC), BIIS (NL, HES), ISIA (IT, HES), NIHS (SE, HES), and FIIT (ES, REC) are public bodies, higher education establishments, or research organisations from EU Member States and are required to hold Gender Equality Plans at the time of grant signature, in compliance with the eligibility criterion in application form Section A.2.",
